class="firstHeading" lang="en">Christopher Nolan</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other people named Christopher Nolan, see <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Christopher Nolan (disambiguation)">Christopher Nolan (disambiguation)</a>.</div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<table class="infobox biography vcard" style="width:22em"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><span class="fn">Christopher Nolan</span></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">\n<a <a href="/wiki/2018_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2018 Cannes Film Festival">2018 Cannes Film Festival</a></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Born</th><td>\n<span class="nickname">Christopher Edward Nolan</span><br /><span style="display:none"> (<span class="bday">1970-07-30</span>) </span>30 July 1970<span class="noprint ForceAgeToShow"> (age&#160;48)</span><br /><span class="birthplace"><a href="/wiki/Westminster" title="Westminster">Westminster</a>, <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England</span></td></tr><tr><th scope="row">Citizenship</th><td class="category">\n<div Joy</a> (sister-in-law)</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>Christopher Edward Nolan</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/\xcb\x88/: primary stress follows">\xcb\x88</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span><span title="/o\xca\x8a/: &#39;o&#39; in &#39;code&#39;">o\xca\x8a</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span><span title="/\xc9\x99/: &#39;a&#39; in &#39;about&#39;">\xc9\x99</span><span title="&#39;n&#39; in &#39;nigh&#39;">n</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born 30 July 1970) is an English <a href="/wiki/Film_director" title="Film director">film director</a>, <a href="/wiki/Screenwriter" title="Screenwriter">screenwriter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Film_producer" title="Film producer">producer</a> who holds both British and American citizenship. He is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_directors" title="List of highest-grossing directors">highest-grossing directors in history</a>, and among the most acclaimed and influential filmmakers of the 21st<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>century.\n</p><p>Having made his directorial debut with <i><a href="/wiki/Following" title="Following">Following</a></i> (1998), Nolan gained considerable attention for his second feature <i><a href="/wiki/Memento_(film)" title="Memento (film)">Memento</a></i> (2000), for which he was nominated for <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Christopher_Nolan" title="List of awards and nominations received by Christopher Nolan">numerous accolades</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Screenplay" title="Academy Award for Best Original Screenplay">Academy Award for Best Original Screenplay</a>. The acclaim garnered by his <a href="/wiki/Independent_films" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent films">independent films</a> gave Nolan the opportunity to make the big-budget thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Insomnia_(2002_film)" title="Insomnia (2002 film)">Insomnia</a></i> (2002) and the mystery drama <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prestige_(film)" title="The Prestige (film)">The Prestige</a></i> (2006). He found further popular and critical success with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Trilogy" class="mw-redirect" title="The Dark Knight Trilogy">The Dark Knight Trilogy</a></i> (2005\xe2\x80\x932012); <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i> (2010),  which received eight Academy Award nominations, including for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> and Best Original Screenplay;  <i><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)">Interstellar</a></i> (2014); and <i><a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_(2017_film)" title="Dunkirk (2017 film)">Dunkirk</a></i> (2017), which earned him his first Academy Award nomination for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Best Director</a>. His ten films have grossed over US$4.7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion worldwide and garnered a total of 34 <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Oscar</a> nominations and ten wins. Nolan has co-written several of his films with his brother <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Nolan" title="Jonathan Nolan">Jonathan</a>, and runs the production company <a href="/wiki/Syncopy_Inc." title="Syncopy Inc.">Syncopy Inc.</a> with his wife <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thomas" title="Emma Thomas">Emma Thomas</a>.\n</p><p>Nolan\'s films are typically rooted in <a href="/wiki/Epistemology" title="Epistemology">epistemological</a> and <a href="/wiki/Metaphysics" title="Metaphysics">metaphysical</a> themes, exploring human morality, the construction of <a href="/wiki/Time" title="Time">time</a>, and the malleable nature of <a href="/wiki/Memory" title="Memory">memory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Personal_identity" title="Personal identity">personal identity</a>. His body of work is permeated by <a href="/wiki/Materialism" title="Materialism">materialistic</a> perspectives, <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_narrative" title="Nonlinear narrative">nonlinear storytelling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Practical_special_effects" class="mw-redirect" title="Practical special effects">practical special effects</a>, innovative soundscapes, large-format film photography, and analogous relationships between visual language and narrative elements. In addition to his filmmaking, he is an advocate for <a href="/wiki/Film_preservation" title="Film preservation">film preservation</a> and the continued availability of <a href="/wiki/Film_stock" title="Film stock">film stock</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:167px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flaxman_Gallery,_UCL.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG/165px-Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG" width="165" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG/247px-Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG/330px-Flaxman_Gallery%2C_UCL.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flaxman_Gallery,_UCL.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nolan attended <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a>, and used its Flaxman Gallery for a scene in <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i> (2010).<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Nolan was born in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, England.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> His English father, Brendan James Nolan, was an advertising executive, and his American mother, Christina (n\xc3\xa9e Jensen), worked as a <a href="/wiki/Flight_attendant" title="Flight attendant">flight attendant</a> and an English teacher.<sup id="cite_ref-Shone2014_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shone2014-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feinberg_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feinberg-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> His childhood was split between London and <a href="/wiki/Evanston,_Illinois" title="Evanston, Illinois">Evanston, Illinois</a>, and he has both British and US citizenship.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boucher_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> He has an older brother, Matthew Francis Nolan, a convicted criminal,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> and a younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Nolan" title="Jonathan Nolan">Jonathan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He began making films at age seven, borrowing his father\'s <a href="/wiki/Super_8_mm_film" class="mw-redirect" title="Super 8 mm film">Super<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>8 camera</a> and shooting short films with his action figures.<sup id="cite_ref-Timberg_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timberg-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Growing up, Nolan was particularly influenced by <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey_(film)" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (film)">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i> (1968) and <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i> (1977).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Around the age of eight, he made a <a href="/wiki/Stop_motion" title="Stop motion">stop motion animation</a> homage to the latter called <i>Space Wars</i>. His uncle, who worked at <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a> building guidance systems for the <a href="/wiki/Apollo_program" title="Apollo program">Apollo</a> rockets, sent him some launch footage: "I re-filmed them off the screen and cut them in, thinking no-one would notice," Nolan later remarked.<sup id="cite_ref-Shone2014_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shone2014-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> From the age of eleven, he aspired to be a professional filmmaker.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span id="1989.E2.80.931997:_Career_beginnings"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1989\xe2\x80\x931997:_Career_beginnings">1989\xe2\x80\x931997: Career beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1989\xe2\x80\x931997: Career beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>When Nolan\'s family relocated to Chicago during his formative years, he started making films with Adrien and <a href="/wiki/Roko_Belic" title="Roko Belic">Roko Belic</a>. He has continued his collaboration with the brothers, receiving a credit for his editorial assistance on their Oscar-nominated documentary <i><a href="/wiki/Genghis_Blues" title="Genghis Blues">Genghis Blues</a></i> (1999).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> Nolan also worked alongside Belic (and future <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize_for_International_Reporting" title="Pulitzer Prize for International Reporting">Pulitzer Prize</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Gettleman" title="Jeffrey Gettleman">Jeffrey Gettleman</a>) on documenting a safari across four African countries, organized by the late photojournalist <a href="/wiki/Dan_Eldon" title="Dan Eldon">Dan Eldon</a> in the early 1990s.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Nolan was educated at <a href="/wiki/Haileybury_and_Imperial_Service_College" title="Haileybury and Imperial Service College">Haileybury and Imperial Service College</a>, an independent school in <a href="/wiki/Hertford_Heath" title="Hertford Heath">Hertford Heath</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hertfordshire" title="Hertfordshire">Hertfordshire</a>, and later read <a href="/wiki/English_literature" title="English literature">English literature</a> at <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a> (UCL). He chose UCL specifically for its filmmaking facilities, which comprised a <a href="/wiki/Steenbeck" title="Steenbeck">Steenbeck editing suite</a> and <a href="/wiki/16_mm_film#Cameras" title="16 mm film">16<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>mm film cameras</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tempest_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tempest-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Nolan was president of the Union\'s Film Society,<sup id="cite_ref-Tempest_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tempest-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and with <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thomas" title="Emma Thomas">Emma Thomas</a> (his girlfriend and future wife) he screened <a href="/wiki/35_mm" class="mw-redirect" title="35 mm">35 mm</a> feature films during the school year and used the money earned to produce <a href="/wiki/16_mm" class="mw-redirect" title="16 mm">16 mm</a> films over the summers.<sup id="cite_ref-British_Cinematographer_pt2_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-British_Cinematographer_pt2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> During his college years, Nolan made two short films. The first was the <a href="/wiki/Surrealism" title="Surrealism">surreal</a> <a href="/wiki/Super_8_film" title="Super 8 film">8<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>mm</a> <i>Tarantella</i> (1989), which was shown on <i>Image Union</i> (an independent film and video showcase on the <a href="/wiki/Public_Broadcasting_Service" class="mw-redirect" title="Public Broadcasting Service">Public Broadcasting Service</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The second was <i>Larceny</i> (1995), filmed over a weekend in black and white with limited equipment and a small cast and crew.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Funded by Nolan and shot with the society\'s equipment, it appeared at the <a href="/wiki/Cambridge_Film_Festival" title="Cambridge Film Festival">Cambridge Film Festival</a> in 1996 and is considered one of UCL\'s best shorts.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After earning his  bachelor\'s degree in English literature in 1993, Nolan worked as a <a href="/wiki/Script_analyst" title="Script analyst">script reader</a>, <a href="/wiki/Camera_operator" title="Camera operator">camera operator</a>, and director of <a href="/wiki/Corporate_video" title="Corporate video">corporate videos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sponsored_film" title="Sponsored film">industrial films</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Tempest_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tempest-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Feinberg_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Feinberg-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> He also made a third short, <i><a href="/wiki/Doodlebug_(film)" title="Doodlebug (film)">Doodlebug</a></i> (1997), about a man chasing an insect around a flat with a shoe, only to discover when killing it that it is a miniature of himself.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> During this period in his career, Nolan had little or no success getting his projects off the ground; he later recalled the "stack of rejection letters" that greeted his early forays into making films, adding "there\'s a very limited pool of finance in the UK. To be honest, it\'s a very clubby kind of place&#160;... Never had any support whatsoever from the British film industry."<sup id="cite_ref-AndrewPulver05_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndrewPulver05-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="1998.E2.80.932004:_Breakthrough"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1998\xe2\x80\x932004:_Breakthrough">1998\xe2\x80\x932004: Breakthrough</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1998\xe2\x80\x932004: Breakthrough">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 1998 Nolan directed his first feature, <i><a href="/wiki/Following" title="Following">Following</a></i>, which he personally funded and filmed with friends.<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> It depicts an unemployed young writer (<a href="/wiki/Jeremy_Theobald" title="Jeremy Theobald">Jeremy Theobald</a>) who trails strangers through London, hoping they will provide material for his first novel, but is drawn into a criminal underworld when he fails to keep his distance. The film was inspired by Nolan\'s experience of living in London and having his flat burgled: "There is an interesting connection between a stranger going through your possessions and the concept of following people at random through a crowd&#160;&#8211;&#32;both take you beyond the boundaries of ordinary <a href="/wiki/Social_relations" class="mw-redirect" title="Social relations">social relations</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> <i>Following</i> was made on a modest budget of \xc2\xa33,000, and was shot on weekends over the course of a year.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> To conserve <a href="/wiki/Film_stock" title="Film stock">film stock</a>, each scene in the film was rehearsed extensively to ensure that the first or second take could be used in the final edit.<sup id="cite_ref-nolandotnet_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nolandotnet-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Tobias_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tobias-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> Co-produced with Emma Thomas and Jeremy Theobald, Nolan wrote, photographed, and edited the film himself.<sup id="cite_ref-nolandotnet_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nolandotnet-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> <i>Following</i> won several awards during its festival run<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> and was well received by critics; <i>The New Yorker</i> wrote that it "echoed <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hitchcock" title="Alfred Hitchcock">Hitchcock</a> classics", but was "leaner and meaner".<sup id="cite_ref-Timberg_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timberg-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Janet_Maslin" title="Janet Maslin">Janet Maslin</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> was impressed with its "spare look" and agile hand-held camerawork, saying, "As a result, the actors convincingly carry off the before, during and after modes that the film eventually, and artfully, weaves together."<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> On 11<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>December 2012 it was released on DVD and <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray" title="Blu-ray">Blu-ray</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Criterion_Collection" class="mw-redirect" title="Criterion Collection">Criterion Collection</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatleft" style="width:246px;&#32;;"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303512">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:0.5em 1.4em 0.8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{margin:0.5em auto 0.8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft p,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright p{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:larger;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9c ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" \xe2\x80\x9d ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:360px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{min-width:100%;margin:0 0 0.8em!important;float:none!important}}</style>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">[The] difference between shooting <i><a href="/wiki/Following" title="Following">Following</a></i> with a group of friends wearing our own clothes and my mum making sandwiches to spending $4&#160;million of somebody else\'s money on <i><a href="/wiki/Memento_(film)" title="Memento (film)">Memento</a></i> and having a crew of a hundred people is, to this day, by far the biggest leap I\'ve ever made.</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Nolan (in 2012) on the jump from his first film to his second.<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>As a result of <i>Following</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s success, Nolan was afforded the opportunity to make his breakthrough hit <i><a href="/wiki/Memento_(film)" title="Memento (film)">Memento</a></i> (2000). During a road trip from Chicago to Los Angeles, his brother Jonathan pitched the idea for "<i><a href="/wiki/Memento_Mori_(short_story)" title="Memento Mori (short story)">Memento Mori</a></i>", about a man with <a href="/wiki/Anterograde_amnesia" title="Anterograde amnesia">anterograde amnesia</a> who uses notes and tattoos to hunt for his wife\'s murderer. Nolan developed a screenplay that told the story in reverse; Aaron Ryder, an executive for <a href="/wiki/Newmarket_Films" title="Newmarket Films">Newmarket Films</a>, said it was "perhaps the most innovative script I had ever seen".<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The film was optioned and given a budget of $4.5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <i>Memento</i>, starring <a href="/wiki/Guy_Pearce" title="Guy Pearce">Guy Pearce</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carrie-Anne_Moss" title="Carrie-Anne Moss">Carrie-Anne Moss</a>, premiered in September 2000 at the <a href="/wiki/Venice_International_Film_Festival" class="mw-redirect" title="Venice International Film Festival">Venice International Film Festival</a> to critical acclaim.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joe_Morgenstern" title="Joe Morgenstern">Joe Morgenstern</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> wrote in his review, "I can\'t remember when a movie has seemed so clever, strangely affecting and slyly funny at the very same time."<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Basil Smith, in the book <i>The Philosophy of Neo-Noir</i>, draws a comparison with <a href="/wiki/John_Locke" title="John Locke">John Locke</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/An_Essay_Concerning_Human_Understanding" title="An Essay Concerning Human Understanding">An Essay Concerning Human Understanding</a></i>, which argues that conscious memories constitute our identities, a theme that Nolan explores in the film.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> The film was a box-office success<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> and received a number of accolades, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Writing_(Original_Screenplay)" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Best Writing (Original Screenplay)">Academy Award</a> and <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Screenplay" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Screenplay">Golden Globe Award</a> nominations for its screenplay, <a href="/wiki/Independent_Spirit_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Independent Spirit Award">Independent Spirit Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Independent_Spirit_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Independent Spirit Award for Best Director">Best Director</a> and <a href="/wiki/Independent_Spirit_Award_for_Best_Screenplay" title="Independent Spirit Award for Best Screenplay">Best Screenplay</a>, and a <a href="/wiki/Directors_Guild_of_America" title="Directors Guild of America">Directors Guild of America</a> (DGA) Award nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimesawards_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimesawards-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <i>Memento</i> was considered by numerous critics to be one of the best films of the <a href="/wiki/2000s_in_film" title="2000s in film">2000s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Metadecade_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metadecade-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the film was selected by the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> for preservation in the United States <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Registry" title="National Film Registry">National Film Registry</a>, being deemed "culturally, historically, or aesthetically significant".<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:148px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_(Mostra).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_%28Mostra%29.jpg/146px-Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_%28Mostra%29.jpg" width="146" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_%28Mostra%29.jpg/220px-Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_%28Mostra%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_%28Mostra%29.jpg/293px-Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_%28Mostra%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="1500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Steven_Soderbergh_66%C3%A8me_Festival_de_Venise_(Mostra).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oscar-winning film director <a href="/wiki/Steven_Soderbergh" title="Steven Soderbergh">Steven Soderbergh</a> <i>(pictured)</i> supported Nolan in his transition to studio filmmaking.</div></div></div>\n<p>Impressed by his work on <i>Memento</i>, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Soderbergh" title="Steven Soderbergh">Steven Soderbergh</a> recruited Nolan to direct the <a href="/wiki/Psychological_thriller" title="Psychological thriller">psychological thriller</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Insomnia_(2002_film)" title="Insomnia (2002 film)">Insomnia</a></i> (2002), starring Academy Award winners <a href="/wiki/Al_Pacino" title="Al Pacino">Al Pacino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robin_Williams" title="Robin Williams">Robin Williams</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hilary_Swank" title="Hilary Swank">Hilary Swank</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-insomnia_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insomnia-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> initially wanted a more seasoned director, but Soderbergh and his <a href="/wiki/Section_Eight_Productions" title="Section Eight Productions">Section Eight Productions</a> fought for Nolan, as well as his choice of cinematographer (<a href="/wiki/Wally_Pfister" title="Wally Pfister">Wally Pfister</a>) and editor (<a href="/wiki/Dody_Dorn" title="Dody Dorn">Dody Dorn</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> With a $46<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million budget, it was described as "a much more conventional Hollywood film than anything the director has done before".<sup id="cite_ref-insomnia_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-insomnia-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> A remake of the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Insomnia_(1997_film)" title="Insomnia (1997 film)">Norwegian film of the same name</a>, <i>Insomnia</i> is about two Los Angeles detectives sent to a northern Alaskan town to investigate the murder of a local teenager. It received positive reviews from critics and performed well at the box office, earning $113<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> Film critic <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> praised the film for introducing new perspectives and ideas on the issues of morality and guilt. "Unlike most remakes, the Nolan <i>Insomnia</i> is not a pale retread, but a re-examination of the material, like a new production of a good play."<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Erik_Skjoldbj%C3%A6rg" title="Erik Skjoldbj\xc3\xa6rg">Erik Skjoldbj\xc3\xa6rg</a>, the director of the original film, was satisfied with Nolan\'s version, calling it a "well crafted, smart film ... with a really good director handling it".<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Schickel" title="Richard Schickel">Richard Schickel</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i> deemed <i>Insomnia</i> a "worthy successor" to <i>Memento</i>, and "a triumph of atmosphere over a none-too-mysterious mystery".<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After <i>Insomnia</i>, Nolan planned a <a href="/wiki/Howard_Hughes" title="Howard Hughes">Howard Hughes</a> biographical film starring <a href="/wiki/Jim_Carrey" title="Jim Carrey">Jim Carrey</a>. He penned a screenplay, which he said was "the best script I\'ve ever written", but when he learned that <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> was making a Hughes biopic (2004\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Aviator_(2004_film)" title="The Aviator (2004 film)">The Aviator</a></i>), he reluctantly tabled his script and moved on to other projects.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> After turning down an offer to direct the historical epic <i><a href="/wiki/Troy_(film)" title="Troy (film)">Troy</a></i> (2004),<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Nolan worked on adapting <a href="/wiki/Ruth_Rendell" title="Ruth Rendell">Ruth Rendell</a>\'s crime novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Keys_to_the_Street" title="The Keys to the Street">The Keys to the Street</a></i> into a screenplay that he planned to direct for <a href="/wiki/Fox_Searchlight_Pictures" title="Fox Searchlight Pictures">Fox Searchlight Pictures</a>, but eventually left the project, citing the similarities to his previous films.<sup id="cite_ref-blogspot_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blogspot-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2005.E2.80.932013:_Mainstream_and_critical_success"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2005\xe2\x80\x932013:_Mainstream_and_critical_success">2005\xe2\x80\x932013: Mainstream and critical success</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2005\xe2\x80\x932013: Mainstream and critical success">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In early 2003 Nolan approached Warner Bros. with the idea of making a new <a href="/wiki/Batman" title="Batman">Batman</a> film. Fascinated by the character and story, he wanted to make a film grounded in a "relatable" world more reminiscent of a classical drama than a comic-book fantasy.<sup id="cite_ref-bb_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bb-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i>, the biggest project Nolan had undertaken to that point,<sup id="cite_ref-bb_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bb-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> premiered in June 2005 to critical acclaim and commercial success.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> Starring <a href="/wiki/Christian_Bale" title="Christian Bale">Christian Bale</a> in the title role, along with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gary_Oldman" title="Gary Oldman">Gary Oldman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Freeman" title="Morgan Freeman">Morgan Freeman</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a>, the film revived the franchise, heralding a trend towards darker films that <a href="/wiki/Reboot_(fiction)" title="Reboot (fiction)">rebooted</a> (or retold) backstories.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> It tells the <a href="/wiki/Origin_story" title="Origin story">origin story</a> of the character from Bruce Wayne\'s initial <a href="/wiki/Fear_of_bats" title="Fear of bats">fear of bats</a>, the death of his parents, his journey to become Batman, and his fight against <a href="/wiki/Ra%27s_al_Ghul" title="Ra&#39;s al Ghul">Ra\'s al Ghul</a>\'s plot to destroy <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a>. Praised for its psychological depth and contemporary relevance,<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kyle_Smith" title="Kyle Smith">Kyle Smith</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="The New York Post">The New York Post</a></i> called it "a wake-up call to the people who keep giving us cute capers about men in tights. It wipes the smirk off the face of the superhero movie."<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> <i>Batman Begins</i> was the eighth-highest-grossing film of 2005 in the United States and the year\'s ninth-highest-grossing film worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> It was nominated for the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography" title="Academy Award for Best Cinematography">Academy Award for Best Cinematography</a> and three <a href="/wiki/BAFTA" class="mw-redirect" title="BAFTA">BAFTA</a> awards.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> On the film\'s 10th anniversary, <i><a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a></i> published an article describing its influence: "Reboot became part of our modern vocabulary, and superhero origin stories became increasingly en<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>vogue for the genre. The phrase "dark and gritty" likewise joined the cinematic lexicon, influencing our perception of different approaches to storytelling not only in the comic book film genre but in all sorts of other genres as well."<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Before returning to the Batman franchise, Nolan directed, co-wrote, and produced <i><a href="/wiki/The_Prestige_(film)" title="The Prestige (film)">The Prestige</a></i> (2006), an adaptation of the <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Priest_(novelist)" title="Christopher Priest (novelist)">Christopher Priest</a> <a href="/wiki/The_Prestige" title="The Prestige">novel</a> about two rival 19th-century magicians.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In 2001, when Nolan was in <a href="/wiki/Post-production" title="Post-production">post-production</a> for <i>Insomnia</i>, he asked his brother Jonathan to help write the script for the film. The screenplay was an intermittent, five-year collaboration between the brothers.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> Nolan initially intended to make the film as early as 2003, postponing the project after agreeing to make <i>Batman Begins</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Starring <a href="/wiki/Hugh_Jackman" title="Hugh Jackman">Hugh Jackman</a> and Christian Bale in the lead roles, <i>The Prestige</i> received critical acclaim (including Oscar nominations for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography" title="Academy Award for Best Cinematography">Best Cinematography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Art_Direction" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Best Art Direction">Best Art Direction</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> and earned over $109<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> described it as "quite a movie&#160;&#8211;&#32;atmospheric, obsessive, almost satanic".<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> called it an "ambitious, unnerving melodrama".<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philip_French" title="Philip French">Philip French</a> wrote in his review for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Guardian" title="The Guardian">The Guardian</a></i>: "In addition to the intellectual or philosophical excitement it engenders, <i>The Prestige</i> is gripping, suspenseful, mysterious, moving and often darkly funny."<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Dark_Knight_European_Premier_-_Leicester_square2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/The_Dark_Knight_European_Premier_-_Leicester_square2.jpg/220px-The_Dark_Knight_European_Premier_-_Leicester_square2.jpg" width="220" height="147" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/The_Dark_Knight_European_Premier_-_Leicester_square2.jpg/330px-The_Dark_Knight_European_Premier_-_Leicester_square2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/The_Dark_Knight_European_Premier_-_Leicester_square2.jpg/440px-The_Dark_Knight_European_Premier_-_Leicester_square2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2428" data-file-height="1623" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">Nolan (left) with the cast and crew of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i> at the 2008 European premiere in London.</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/220px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg" width="220" height="120" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/330px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/440px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1004" data-file-height="546" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The cast of <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i> at the premiere in July 2010.</div></div></div></div>\n<p>In July 2006 Nolan announced that the follow-up to <i>Batman Begins</i> would be called <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Approaching the sequel, Nolan wanted to expand on the <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">noirish</a> quality of the first film by broadening the canvas and taking on "the dynamic of a story of the city, a large crime story<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... where you\'re looking at the police, the justice system, the vigilante, the poor people, the rich people, the criminals".<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Released in 2008 to great critical acclaim, <i>The Dark Knight</i> has been cited as one of the best films of the 2000s and one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_films_considered_the_best#Comic_book/superhero" title="List of films considered the best">best superhero films ever made</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Metadecade_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Metadecade-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Paste_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paste-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Empiredecade_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Empiredecade-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Manohla_Dargis" title="Manohla Dargis">Manohla Dargis</a> of <i>The New York Times</i> found the film to be of higher artistic merit than many Hollywood blockbusters: "Pitched at the divide between art and industry, poetry and entertainment, it goes darker and deeper than any Hollywood movie of its comic-book kind."<sup id="cite_ref-Dargis_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dargis-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Ebert expressed a similar point of view, describing it as a "haunted film that leaps beyond its origins and becomes an engrossing tragedy."<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Smith" title="Kevin Smith">Kevin Smith</a> called it "the <i>Godfather [Part] II</i> of comic book films".<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Dark Knight</i> set a number of box-office records during its theatrical run,<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> earning $534,858,444 in North America and $469,700,000 abroad, for a worldwide total of $1,004,558,444.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> It is the first commercial feature film shot partially in the 15/70<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>mm <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> format.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/81st_Academy_Awards" title="81st Academy Awards">81st Academy Awards</a>, the film was nominated for eight Oscars, winning two: the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">Academy Award for Best Sound Editing</a> and a posthumous <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor</a> for <a href="/wiki/Heath_Ledger" title="Heath Ledger">Heath Ledger</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Nolan was recognised by his peers with nominations from the <a href="/wiki/Directors_Guild_of_America" title="Directors Guild of America">DGA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Writers_Guild_of_America" title="Writers Guild of America">Writers Guild of America</a> (WGA), and <a href="/wiki/Producers_Guild_of_America" title="Producers Guild of America">Producers Guild of America</a> (PGA).<sup id="cite_ref-nytimesawards_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimesawards-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Ten years after its release, <a href="/wiki/Bilge_Ebiri" title="Bilge Ebiri">Bilge Ebiri</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Village_Voice" title="The Village Voice">The Village Voice</a></i> wrote, "Its politics have been discussed ad infinitum. Its stylistic influence has become ubiquitous, then pass\xc3\xa9, then somehow aspirational ... <i>The Dark Knight</i> is perhaps the most powerful exploration of guilt the modern American blockbuster has given us."<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After <i>The Dark Knight</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s success, Warner Bros. signed Nolan to direct <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i>. Nolan also wrote and co-produced the film, described as "a contemporary sci-fi actioner set within the architecture of the mind".<sup id="cite_ref-Tackles_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tackles-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> Before being released in theaters, critics such as <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lou_Lumenick" title="Lou Lumenick">Lou Lumenick</a> wondered if Nolan\'s faith in moviegoers\' intelligence would cost him at the box office.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> Starring a large ensemble cast led by <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>, the film was released on 16<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>July 2010, and was a critical and commercial success.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Roeper" title="Richard Roeper">Richard Roeper</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> awarded the film a perfect score of "A+" and called it "one of the best movies of the [21st] century".<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kermode" title="Mark Kermode">Mark Kermode</a> named it the best film of 2010, stating "<i>Inception</i> is proof that people are not stupid, that cinema is not trash, and that it is possible for blockbusters and art to be the same thing."<sup id="cite_ref-Kermode_95-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kermode-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Schuker_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schuker-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The film ended up grossing over $820<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million worldwide<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> and was nominated for eight Oscars, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Screenplay" title="Academy Award for Best Original Screenplay">Best Original Screenplay</a>; it won the award for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography" title="Academy Award for Best Cinematography">Best Cinematography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award for Best Sound">Best Sound Mixing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">Best Sound Editing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Academy_Awards_2010_(83rd)_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Academy_Awards_2010_(83rd)-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Nolan also received <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_of_Film_and_Television_Arts" title="British Academy of Film and Television Arts">BAFTA</a>, Golden Globe, DGA, and PGA Award nominations, as well as a WGA Award for his work on the film.<sup id="cite_ref-nytimesawards_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nytimesawards-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> While in post-production on <i>Inception</i>, Nolan gave an interview for <i><a href="/wiki/These_Amazing_Shadows" title="These Amazing Shadows">These Amazing Shadows</a></i> (2011), a documentary spotlighting film appreciation and preservation by the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Registry" title="National Film Registry">National Film Registry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> He also appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Side_by_Side_(2012_film)" title="Side by Side (2012 film)">Side by Side</a></i> (2012), a documentary about the history, process, and workflow of both digital and photochemical film creation.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2012 Nolan directed his third and final Batman film, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises" title="The Dark Knight Rises">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i>. Although he was initially hesitant about returning to the series, he agreed to come back after developing a story with his brother and <a href="/wiki/David_S._Goyer" title="David S. Goyer">David S. Goyer</a> that he felt would end the series on a high note.<sup id="cite_ref-Bettinger_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bettinger-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> was released on 20<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>July 2012 to positive reviews; Andrew O\'Hehir of <i><a href="/wiki/Salon_(website)" title="Salon (website)">Salon</a></i> called it "arguably the biggest, darkest, most thrilling and disturbing and utterly balls-out spectacle ever created for the screen", further describing the work as "auteurist spectacle on a scale never before possible and never before attempted".<sup id="cite_ref-Hehir_103-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hehir-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Christy_Lemire" title="Christy Lemire">Christy Lemire</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Associated_Press" class="mw-redirect" title="The Associated Press">The Associated Press</a></i> wrote in her review that Nolan concluded his trilogy in a "typically spectacular, ambitious fashion", but disliked the "overloaded" story and excessive grimness, saying, "This is the problem when you\'re an exceptional, visionary filmmaker. When you give people something extraordinary, they expect it every time. Anything short of that feels like a letdown."<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Like its predecessor, it performed well at the box office, becoming the thirteenth film in the world to gross over $1<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>billion.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> During a midnight showing of the film at the Century<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>16 cinema in <a href="/wiki/Aurora,_Colorado" title="Aurora, Colorado">Aurora, Colorado</a>, <a href="/wiki/2012_Aurora_shooting" title="2012 Aurora shooting">a gunman opened fire inside the theater</a>, killing 12 people and injuring 58 others.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Nolan released a statement to the press expressing his condolences for the victims of what he described as a senseless tragedy.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Nolan,_London,_2013_(crop).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Christopher_Nolan%2C_London%2C_2013_%28crop%29.jpg/170px-Christopher_Nolan%2C_London%2C_2013_%28crop%29.jpg" width="170" height="249" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Christopher_Nolan%2C_London%2C_2013_%28crop%29.jpg/255px-Christopher_Nolan%2C_London%2C_2013_%28crop%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Christopher_Nolan%2C_London%2C_2013_%28crop%29.jpg/340px-Christopher_Nolan%2C_London%2C_2013_%28crop%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="634" data-file-height="929" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Nolan,_London,_2013_(crop).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nolan at the 2013 premiere of <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i> in London</div></div></div>\n<p>During story discussions for <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> in 2010, Goyer told Nolan of his idea to present <a href="/wiki/Superman" title="Superman">Superman</a> in a modern context.<sup id="cite_ref-GoyStory_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoyStory-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup> Impressed with Goyer\'s <a href="/wiki/First_contact_(science_fiction)" title="First contact (science fiction)">first contact</a> concept, Nolan pitched the idea for <i><a href="/wiki/Man_of_Steel_(film)" title="Man of Steel (film)">Man of Steel</a></i> (2013) to Warner Bros,<sup id="cite_ref-GoyStory_109-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GoyStory-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> who hired Nolan to produce and Goyer to write.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> Nolan offered <a href="/wiki/Zack_Snyder" title="Zack Snyder">Zack Snyder</a> to direct the film, based on his stylized adaptations of <i><a href="/wiki/300_(film)" title="300 (film)">300</a></i> (2007) and <i><a href="/wiki/Watchmen_(film)" title="Watchmen (film)">Watchmen</a></i> (2009) and his "innate aptitude for dealing with superheroes as real characters".<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> Starring <a href="/wiki/Henry_Cavill" title="Henry Cavill">Henry Cavill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Amy_Adams" title="Amy Adams">Amy Adams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Costner" title="Kevin Costner">Kevin Costner</a>, <a href="/wiki/Russell_Crowe" title="Russell Crowe">Russell Crowe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Shannon" title="Michael Shannon">Michael Shannon</a>, <i>Man of Steel</i> grossed more than $660<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million at the worldwide box office, but received a divided critical reaction.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> However, Nolan was thoroughly impressed by Snyder\'s work, saying that the director "knocked it out of the park", and believed the film would have the same potential to excite audiences as when he himself saw the <a href="/wiki/Superman_(1978_film)" title="Superman (1978 film)">Christopher Reeve version</a> in 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="2014.E2.80.93present:_Large-scale_epics_and_film_preservation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="2014\xe2\x80\x93present:_Large-scale_epics_and_film_preservation">2014\xe2\x80\x93present: Large-scale epics and film preservation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2014\xe2\x80\x93present: Large-scale epics and film preservation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In 2014 Nolan and Emma Thomas served as <a href="/wiki/Executive_producer" title="Executive producer">executive producers</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Transcendence_(2014_film)" title="Transcendence (2014 film)">Transcendence</a></i>, the directorial debut of Nolan\'s longtime cinematographer Wally Pfister.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> Starring <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Depp" title="Johnny Depp">Johnny Depp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rebecca_Hall" title="Rebecca Hall">Rebecca Hall</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bettany" title="Paul Bettany">Paul Bettany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kate_Mara" title="Kate Mara">Kate Mara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cillian_Murphy" title="Cillian Murphy">Cillian Murphy</a>, and Morgan Freeman, <i>Transcendence</i> was released in theaters on 18<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>April 2014 to mostly unfavorable reviews and disappointing box office results.<sup id="cite_ref-Transcendence14_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Transcendence14-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> A.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>A. Dowd of <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> gave the film a C- rating, pointing out that "[Pfister] lacks Nolan\'s talent for weaving grand pop spectacle out of cultural anxieties."<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/170px-Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" width="170" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/255px-Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg/340px-Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2022" data-file-height="2622" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Jonathan_Nolan_by_Gage_Skidmore.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nolan\'s younger brother, <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Nolan" title="Jonathan Nolan">Jonathan</a>, co-wrote the screenplay for <i>Interstellar</i>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Nolan also directed, wrote, and produced the science-fiction film <i><a href="/wiki/Interstellar_(film)" title="Interstellar (film)">Interstellar</a></i> (2014). The first drafts of the script were written by Jonathan Nolan, and it was originally to be directed by <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup> Based on the scientific theories of renowned <a href="/wiki/Theoretical_physicist" class="mw-redirect" title="Theoretical physicist">theoretical physicist</a> <a href="/wiki/Kip_Thorne" title="Kip Thorne">Kip Thorne</a>, the film depicted "a heroic interstellar voyage to the farthest borders of our scientific understanding".<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> <i>Interstellar</i> starred <a href="/wiki/Matthew_McConaughey" title="Matthew McConaughey">Matthew McConaughey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Anne_Hathaway" title="Anne Hathaway">Anne Hathaway</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessica_Chastain" title="Jessica Chastain">Jessica Chastain</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bill_Irwin" title="Bill Irwin">Bill Irwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Burstyn" title="Ellen Burstyn">Ellen Burstyn</a>, and was notably Nolan\'s first collaboration with cinematographer <a href="/wiki/Hoyte_van_Hoytema" title="Hoyte van Hoytema">Hoyte van Hoytema</a>. Paramount Pictures and Warner Bros. co-financed and co-distributed the project, released on 5<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>November 2014 to largely positive reviews and strong box office results, grossing over $670<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> wrote, in his review for <i>The New York Times</i>, "<i>Interstellar</i>, full of visual dazzle, thematic ambition<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... is a sweeping, futuristic adventure driven by grief, dread and regret."<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Berardinelli" title="James Berardinelli">James Berardinelli</a> of <i>Reelviews</i> opined that the film deserved the label of an "experience", and that it was a "unique and mesmerizing" movie.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> Documentary filmmaker <a href="/wiki/Toni_Myers" title="Toni Myers">Toni Myers</a> said of the film, "I loved it because it tackled the most difficult part of human exploration, which is that it\'s a multi-generational journey. It was a real work of art."<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup> <i>Interstellar</i> was particularly praised for its scientific accuracy, which led to the publication of two <a href="/wiki/Scientific_papers" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific papers">scientific papers</a> and the <a href="/wiki/American_Journal_of_Physics" title="American Journal of Physics">American Journal of Physics</a> calling for it to be shown in school science lessons.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup> It was named one of the best films of the year by The <a href="/wiki/American_Film_Institute" title="American Film Institute">American Film Institute</a> (AFI).<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/87th_Academy_Awards" title="87th Academy Awards">87th Academy Awards</a>, the film won <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a> and received four other nominations&#160;&#8211;&#32;<a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Academy Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Score</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Mixing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Mixing">Best Sound Mixing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">Best Sound Editing</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Production_Design" title="Academy Award for Best Production Design">Best Production Design</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup> Nolan curated the short film <i>Emic: A Time Capsule From the People of Earth</i> (2015). It was specifically inspired by the themes of <i>Interstellar</i>, and "attempts to capture and celebrate the human experience on Earth".<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2015 Nolan\'s production company Syncopy formed a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Zeitgeist_Films" title="Zeitgeist Films">Zeitgeist Films</a>, to release Blu-ray editions of Zeitgeist\'s prestige titles. Their first project was <i><a href="/wiki/Elena_(2011_film)" title="Elena (2011 film)">Elena</a></i> (2011) from director <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Zvyagintsev" title="Andrey Zvyagintsev">Andrey Zvyagintsev</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup> As part of a Blu-ray release of the <a href="/wiki/Brothers_Quay" title="Brothers Quay">Quay brothers</a> animated work, Nolan directed the documentary short <i><a href="/wiki/Quay_(film)" title="Quay (film)">Quay</a></i> (2015). He also initiated a theatrical tour, showcasing the Quays\' <i><a href="/wiki/In_Absentia_(film)" title="In Absentia (film)">In Absentia</a></i>, <i>The Comb</i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Street_of_Crocodiles" title="Street of Crocodiles">Street of Crocodiles</a></i>. The program and Nolan\'s short received critical acclaim, with <i><a href="/wiki/Indiewire" class="mw-redirect" title="Indiewire">Indiewire</a></i> writing in their review that the brothers "will undoubtedly have hundreds, if not thousands more fans because of Nolan, and for that <i>The Quay Brothers in 35mm</i> will always be one of latter\'s most important contributions to cinema".<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> In 2015 Nolan joined <a href="/wiki/The_Film_Foundation" title="The Film Foundation">The Film Foundation</a>\'s board of directors, a <a href="/wiki/Non-profit_organization" class="mw-redirect" title="Non-profit organization">non-profit organization</a> dedicated to <a href="/wiki/Film_preservation" title="Film preservation">film preservation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup> Having been instrumental in keeping <a href="/wiki/Kodak" title="Kodak">Kodak</a> and the production of film stock alive in the 2010s, Nolan and visual artist <a href="/wiki/Tacita_Dean" title="Tacita Dean">Tacita Dean</a> invited representatives from leading American film archives, labs, and presenting institutions to participate in an informal summit entitled <i>Reframing the Future of Film</i> at the <a href="/wiki/J._Paul_Getty_Museum" title="J. Paul Getty Museum">Getty Museum</a> in March 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-filmvsdigital_2_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmvsdigital_2-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup> Subsequent events were held at <a href="/wiki/Tate_Modern" title="Tate Modern">Tate Modern</a> in London, <a href="/wiki/Museo_Rufino_Tamayo,_Mexico_City" title="Museo Rufino Tamayo, Mexico City">Museo Tamayo</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">Mexico City</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tata_Theatre" title="Tata Theatre">Tata Theatre</a> in <a href="/wiki/Mumbai" title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> On 7<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>May it was announced that Nolan and <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> had been appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Congress" title="Library of Congress">Library of Congress</a> to serve on the <a href="/wiki/National_Film_Preservation_Board" title="National Film Preservation Board">National Film Preservation Board</a> (NFPB) as DGA representatives.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Later that year, he was featured in the documentary <i>Cinema Futures</i> (2016) by Austrian filmmaker Michael Palm.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> Nolan and Thomas opted to take a step back and only serve as executive producers on Zack Snyder\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_v_Superman:_Dawn_of_Justice" title="Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice">Batman v Superman: Dawn of Justice</a></i> (2016) and <i><a href="/wiki/Justice_League_(film)" title="Justice League (film)">Justice League</a></i> (2017), the sequels to <i>Man of Steel</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-BSExec_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BSExec-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2017 Nolan directed and produced <i><a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_(2017_film)" title="Dunkirk (2017 film)">Dunkirk</a></i>, based on his own original screenplay. The story is set amid <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk_evacuation" title="Dunkirk evacuation">evacuation</a> of <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> soldiers from the beaches of <a href="/wiki/Dunkirk" title="Dunkirk">Dunkirk</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, in 1940. During the year-long production of his first film, <i>Following</i> (1998), Nolan and Thomas hired a small sailing boat to take them across the <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">English Channel</a> and retrace the journey of the <a href="/wiki/Little_ships_of_Dunkirk" class="mw-redirect" title="Little ships of Dunkirk">little ships of Dunkirk</a>. "We did it at the same time of year to get a sense of what it was like, and it turned out to be an incredibly dangerous experience. And that was with no bombs dropping on us."<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> For <i>Dunkirk</i>, Nolan said he was inspired by the work of <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bresson" title="Robert Bresson">Robert Bresson</a>, silent films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Intolerance_(film)" title="Intolerance (film)">Intolerance</a></i> (1916) and <i><a href="/wiki/Sunrise:_A_Song_of_Two_Humans" title="Sunrise: A Song of Two Humans">Sunrise: A Song of Two Humans</a></i> (1927), as well as by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wages_of_Fear" title="The Wages of Fear">The Wages of Fear</a></i> (1953).<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup> Describing the film as a survival tale with a <a href="/wiki/Triptych" title="Triptych">triptych</a> structure, he wanted to make a "sensory, almost experimental movie" with minimal dialogue.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> Nolan said he waited to make <i>Dunkirk</i> until he had earned the trust of a major studio to let him make it as a British film, but with an American budget.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> Before filming, Nolan also sought advice from Spielberg, who later said in an interview with <i>Variety</i>, "Knowing and respecting that Chris [Nolan] is one of the world\'s most imaginative filmmakers, my advice to him was to leave his imagination, as I did on <a href="/wiki/Saving_Private_Ryan" title="Saving Private Ryan"><i>Ryan</i></a>, in second position to the research he was doing to authentically acquit this historical drama."<sup id="cite_ref-LangVariety_150-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LangVariety-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> Starring <a href="/wiki/Fionn_Whitehead" title="Fionn Whitehead">Fionn Whitehead</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lowden" title="Jack Lowden">Jack Lowden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aneurin_Barnard" title="Aneurin Barnard">Aneurin Barnard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harry_Styles" title="Harry Styles">Harry Styles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mark_Rylance" title="Mark Rylance">Mark Rylance</a>, Cillian Murphy, and <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Branagh" title="Kenneth Branagh">Kenneth Branagh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dunkirk</i> was released in theaters on 21<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>July 2017 to widespread critical acclaim and strong box office results,<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup> grossing over $525<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>million worldwide, making it the highest-grossing World War<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>II film of all time. In his review, <a href="/wiki/Mick_LaSalle" title="Mick LaSalle">Mick LaSalle</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Chronicle" title="San Francisco Chronicle">San Francisco Chronicle</a></i> wrote: "It\'s one of the best <a href="/wiki/War_film" title="War film">war films</a> ever made, distinct in its look, in its approach and in the effect it has on viewers. There are movies\xe2\x80\x94they are rare\xe2\x80\x94that lift you out of your present circumstances and immerse you so fully in another experience that you watch in a state of jaw-dropped awe. <i>Dunkirk</i> is that kind of movie." Manohla Dargis of <i>The New York Times</i> lauded the film, calling it "a tour de<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>force of cinematic craft and technique, but one that is unambiguously in the service of a sober, sincere, profoundly moral story that closes the distance between yesterday\'s fights and today\'s."<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> <i>Dunkirk</i> received eight nominations at the <a href="/wiki/71st_British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="71st British Academy Film Awards">71st British Academy Film Awards</a>; winning one for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Sound" title="BAFTA Award for Best Sound">Best Sound</a>, three at the <a href="/wiki/75th_Golden_Globe_Awards" title="75th Golden Globe Awards">75th Golden Globes</a>, and eight at the <a href="/wiki/90th_Academy_Awards" title="90th Academy Awards">90th Academy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Picture" title="Academy Award for Best Picture">Best Picture</a> and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Director" title="Academy Award for Best Director">Best Director</a> (Nolan\'s first Oscar nomination for directing); winning three for Best Sound Editing, Best Sound Mixing, and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Film_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Film Editing">Best Film Editing</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Oscars-18_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Oscars-18-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bafta-18_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bafta-18-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Globes-18_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Globes-18-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup> Nolan was also nominated by the DGA and PGA, among <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Dunkirk" title="List of accolades received by Dunkirk">other accolades</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DGA-18_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DGA-18-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PGA-2018_160-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PGA-2018-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Cannes_2018_4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Cannes_2018_4.jpg/250px-Cannes_2018_4.jpg" width="250" height="125" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Cannes_2018_4.jpg/375px-Cannes_2018_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6e/Cannes_2018_4.jpg/500px-Cannes_2018_4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="638" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Cannes_2018_4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nolan (right) with <a href="/wiki/Keir_Dullea" title="Keir Dullea">Keir Dullea</a>, Katharina Kubrick, and <a href="/wiki/Jan_Harlan" title="Jan Harlan">Jan Harlan</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2018 Cannes Film Festival">2018 Cannes Film Festival</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the months following the <a href="/wiki/Oscar_season" title="Oscar season">Oscar season</a>, Nolan began supervising a new 70mm print of <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey_(film)" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (film)">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i> (1968), made from the <a href="/wiki/Original_camera_negative" title="Original camera negative">original camera negative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup> He presented the film at the <a href="/wiki/2018_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2018 Cannes Film Festival">2018 Cannes Film Festival</a>, with members of Kubrick\'s family in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup> While in Cannes, Nolan also held a two-hour masterclass at the <a href="/wiki/Palais_des_Festivals_et_des_Congr%C3%A8s" title="Palais des Festivals et des Congr\xc3\xa8s">Palais des Festivals</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> observed that the director was greeted "like a rock star", and with a prolonged standing ovation.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> After the premiere, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> released the "unrestored" prints in a select few locations to both critical and commercial success.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> In the spring of 2018, Nolan was featured in
