<a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>\'s <i>Story of Science Fiction</i>, a documentary series about the science fiction genre.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmmaking">Filmmaking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Filmmaking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Aesthetics">Aesthetics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Aesthetics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Regarded as an <a href="/wiki/Auteur" title="Auteur">auteur</a> filmmaker,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup> Nolan\'s visual style often emphasises <a href="/wiki/Urban_area" title="Urban area">urban settings</a>, men in suits, muted colours, dialogue scenes framed in wide close-up with a <a href="/wiki/Shallow_depth_of_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Shallow depth of field">shallow depth of field</a>, and modern locations and architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup> Aesthetically, the director favours deep, evocative shadows, documentary-style lighting, natural settings, and <a href="/wiki/Location_shooting" title="Location shooting">real filming locations</a> over studio work.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> Nolan has noted that many of his films are heavily influenced by <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> He has continuously experimented with <a href="/wiki/Metafiction" title="Metafiction">metafictive elements</a>, <a href="/wiki/Time" title="Time">temporal</a> shifts, elliptical cutting, <a href="/wiki/Solipsism" title="Solipsism">solipsistic perspectives</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nonlinear_narrative" title="Nonlinear narrative">nonlinear storytelling</a>, <a href="/wiki/Labyrinth" title="Labyrinth">labyrinthine</a> plots, and the merging of style and form.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_171-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Leftfield_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leftfield-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bordwell2012_173-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bordwell2012-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> Discussing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Tree_of_Life_(film)" title="The Tree of Life (film)">The Tree of Life</a></i> (2011), Nolan spoke of <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Malick" title="Terrence Malick">Terrence Malick</a>\'s work and how it has influenced his own approach to style, "When you think of a visual style, when you think of the visual language of a film, there tends to be a natural separation of the visual style and the narrative elements. But with the greats, whether it\'s Stanley Kubrick or Terrence Malick or <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Hitchcock" title="Alfred Hitchcock">Hitchcock</a>, what you\'re seeing is an inseparable, a vital relationship between the image and the story it\'s telling".<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Memento_Timeline.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Memento_Timeline.png/170px-Memento_Timeline.png" width="170" height="119" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Memento_Timeline.png/255px-Memento_Timeline.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/Memento_Timeline.png/340px-Memento_Timeline.png 2x" data-file-width="1800" data-file-height="1260" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Memento_Timeline.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A map showing the structure of <i>Memento</i> (2000)</div></div></div>\n<p>Drawing attention to the intrinsically manipulative nature of the medium, Nolan uses narrative and stylistic techniques (notably <a href="/wiki/Mise_en_abyme" title="Mise en abyme">mise en abyme</a> and <a href="/wiki/Recursion" title="Recursion">recursions</a>) to stimulate the viewer to ask themselves why his films are put together in such ways and why the films provoke particular responses.<sup id="cite_ref-Film-philosophy_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Film-philosophy-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> He sometimes uses editing as a way to represent the characters\' psychological states, merging their subjectivity with that of the audience.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> For example, in <i>Memento</i> the fragmented sequential order of scenes is to put the audience into a similar experience of Leonard\'s defective ability to create new long-term memories. In <i>The Prestige</i>, the series of magic tricks and themes of duality and deception mirror the structural narrative of the film.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_171-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> His writing style incorporates a number of <a href="/wiki/Literary_technique" class="mw-redirect" title="Literary technique">storytelling techniques</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Flashback_(narrative)" title="Flashback (narrative)">flashbacks</a>, shifting points of view, and <a href="/wiki/Unreliable_narrator" title="Unreliable narrator">unreliable narrators</a>. Scenes are often interrupted by the unconventional editing style of cutting away quickly from the <a href="/wiki/Money_shot" title="Money shot">money shot</a> (or nearly cutting off characters\' dialogue) and <a href="/wiki/Crosscutting" class="mw-redirect" title="Crosscutting">crosscutting</a> several scenes of parallel action to build to a climax.<sup id="cite_ref-Bevan_171-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bevan-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Embedded narratives and crosscutting between different time frames is a major component of Nolan\'s auteurship. <i>Following</i> contains four timelines and intercuts three. <i>Memento</i> intercuts two timelines, with one moving backward. <i>The Prestige</i> contains four timelines and intercuts three. <i>Inception</i> intercuts four  timelines, all of them framed by a fifth.<sup id="cite_ref-Bordwell2010_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bordwell2010-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Dunkirk</i>, Nolan structured three different timelines to emulate a <a href="/wiki/Shepard_tone" title="Shepard tone">shepard tone</a> in such a way that it "provides a continual feeling of intensity".<sup id="cite_ref-ZimmerNolan_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZimmerNolan-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Noted <a href="/wiki/Film_theory" title="Film theory">film theorist</a> and <a href="/wiki/Film_historian" class="mw-redirect" title="Film historian">historian</a> <a href="/wiki/David_Bordwell" title="David Bordwell">David Bordwell</a> wrote, "For Nolan, I think, form has centrally to do with the sorts of juxtapositions you can create by crosscutting. You could say he treats crosscutting the way <a href="/wiki/Max_Oph%C3%BCls" title="Max Oph\xc3\xbcls">Oph\xc3\xbcls</a> treats <a href="/wiki/Tracking_shot" title="Tracking shot">tracking shots</a> or <a href="/wiki/Carl_Theodor_Dreyer" title="Carl Theodor Dreyer">Dreyer</a> treats stark <a href="/wiki/Interior_design" title="Interior design">decor</a>: an initial commitment to a creative choice, which in turn shapes the handling of story, staging, performance and other factors."<sup id="cite_ref-Bordwell2010_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bordwell2010-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Bordwell further added, "It\'s rare to find any mainstream director so relentlessly focused on exploring a particular batch of storytelling techniques<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... Nolan zeroes in, from film to film, on a few narrative devices, finding new possibilities in what most directors handle routinely. He seems to me a very thoughtful, almost theoretical director in his fascination with turning certain conventions this way and that, to reveal their unexpected possibilities."<sup id="cite_ref-BordwellDunkirk_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BordwellDunkirk-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nolan has also stressed the importance of establishing a clear <a href="/wiki/Narrative_mode" class="mw-redirect" title="Narrative mode">point of view</a> in his films, and makes frequent use of "the shot that walks into a room behind a character, because<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... that takes [the viewer] inside the way that the character enters".<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> On narrative perspective, Nolan has said, "You don\'t want to be hanging above the <a href="/wiki/Maze" title="Maze">maze</a> watching the characters make the wrong choices because it\'s frustrating. You actually want to be in the maze with them, making the turns at their side."<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> Nolan has also used <a href="/wiki/Cin%C3%A9ma-v%C3%A9rit%C3%A9" class="mw-redirect" title="Cin\xc3\xa9ma-v\xc3\xa9rit\xc3\xa9">cin\xc3\xa9ma-v\xc3\xa9rit\xc3\xa9</a> techniques (such as hand-held camera work) to convey realism.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> In an interview at the <a href="/wiki/Film_Society_of_Lincoln_Center" title="Film Society of Lincoln Center">Film Society of Lincoln Center</a>, he explained his emphasis on realism in <i>The Dark Knight</i> trilogy: "You try and get the audience to invest in cinematic reality. When I talk about reality in these films, it\'s often misconstrued as a direct reality, but it\'s really about a cinematic reality."<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In collaboration with composer <a href="/wiki/David_Julyan" title="David Julyan">David Julyan</a>, Nolan\'s films featured slow and atmospheric scores with minimalistic expressions and <a href="/wiki/Ambient_music" title="Ambient music">ambient</a> textures. In the mid-2000s, starting with <i>Batman Begins</i>, Nolan began working with <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>, who is known for integrating <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electronic music</a> with traditional orchestral arrangements. With Zimmer, the soundscape in Nolan\'s films evolved into becoming increasingly more lush, kinetic and experimental.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> An example of this is the main theme from <i>Inception</i>, which is derived from a slowed down version of <a href="/wiki/Edith_Piaf" class="mw-redirect" title="Edith Piaf">Edith Piaf</a>\'s song <a href="/wiki/Non,_je_ne_regrette_rien" title="Non, je ne regrette rien">Non, je ne regrette rien</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ZimmerNolan_180-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZimmerNolan-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> For 2014\'s <i>Interstellar</i>, Zimmer and Nolan wanted to move in a new direction: "The textures, the music, and the sounds, and the thing we sort of created has sort of seeped into other people\'s movies a bit, so it\'s time to reinvent."<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> The score for <i>Dunkirk</i> was written to accommodate the <a href="/wiki/Auditory_illusion" title="Auditory illusion">auditory illusion</a> of a Shepard tone. It was also based on a recording of Nolan\'s own <a href="/wiki/Pocket_watch" title="Pocket watch">pocket watch</a>, which he sent to Zimmer to be <a href="/wiki/Synthesizer" title="Synthesizer">synthesised</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ZimmerNolan_180-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ZimmerNolan-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> Responding to some criticism over his experimental <a href="/wiki/Audio_mixing" title="Audio mixing">sound mix</a> for <i>Interstellar</i>, Nolan remarked, "I\'ve always loved films that approach sound in an impressionistic way and that is an unusual approach for a mainstream blockbuster ... I don\'t agree with the idea that you can only achieve clarity through dialogue. Clarity of story, clarity of emotions \xe2\x80\x94 I try to achieve that in a very layered way using all the different things at my disposal \xe2\x80\x94 picture and sound."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Method">Method</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Method">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:246px;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">Films are subjective \xe2\x80\x93 what you like, what you don\'t like, but the thing for me that is absolutely unifying is the idea that every time I go to the cinema and pay my money and sit down and watch a film go up onscreen, I want to feel that the people who made that film think it\'s the best movie in the world, that they poured everything into it and they really love it. Whether or not I agree with what they\'ve done, I want that effort there&#160;\xe2\x80\x93 I want that sincerity. And when you don\'t feel it, that\'s the only time I feel like I\'m wasting my time at the movies.<sup id="cite_ref-FoundasInception_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoundasInception-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup></div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Nolan, on sincerity and ambition in filmmaking.</cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>Nolan has described his filmmaking process as a combination of intuition and geometry. "I draw a lot of diagrams when I work. I do a lot of thinking about etchings by <a href="/wiki/M._C._Escher" title="M. C. Escher">Escher</a>, for instance. That frees me, finding a mathematical model or a scientific model. I\'ll draw pictures and diagrams that illustrate the movement or the rhythm that I\'m after."<sup id="cite_ref-Cox_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_Technology" title="California Institute of Technology">Caltech</a> physicist and Nobel Laureate Kip Thorne compared Nolan\'s intuition to scientists such as <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>, noting that the director intuitively grasped things non-scientists rarely understand.<sup id="cite_ref-ThorneNolan_190-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThorneNolan-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> Regarding his own decision-making of whether or not to start work on a project, Nolan has proclaimed a belief in the sincerity of his passion for something within the particular project in question as a basis for his selective thought.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> A famously secretive filmmaker, Nolan is also known for his tight security on scripts, even going as far as telling the actors of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i> the ending of the film verbally to avoid any leaks and also keeping the <i>Interstellar</i> plot secret from his composer Hans Zimmer.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>He prefers shooting on <a href="/wiki/Film_stock" title="Film stock">film</a> to <a href="/wiki/Digital_video" title="Digital video">digital video</a>, and opposes the use of <a href="/wiki/Digital_intermediate" title="Digital intermediate">digital intermediates</a> and <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinematography" title="Digital cinematography">digital cinematography</a>, which he feels are less reliable than film and offer inferior image quality. In particular, the director advocates for the use of higher-quality, larger-format film stock such as <a href="/wiki/Anamorphic_format" title="Anamorphic format">anamorphic 35<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>mm</a>, <a href="/wiki/VistaVision" title="VistaVision">VistaVision</a>, <a href="/wiki/70_mm_film" title="70 mm film">65<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>mm</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Weintraub_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> Nolan uses <a href="/wiki/Multiple-camera_setup" title="Multiple-camera setup">multi-camera</a> for stunts and <a href="/wiki/Single-camera_setup" title="Single-camera setup">single-camera</a> for all the dramatic action, from which he then watches <a href="/wiki/Dailies" title="Dailies">dailies</a> every night, saying, "Shooting single-camera means I\'ve already seen every frame as it\'s gone through the <a href="/wiki/Film_gate" title="Film gate">gate</a> because my attention isn\'t divided to multi-cameras."<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He deliberately works under a tight schedule during the early stages of the editing process, forcing himself and his editor to work more spontaneously. "I always think of editing as instinctive or impressionist. Not to think too much, in a way, and feel it more."<sup id="cite_ref-Cox_189-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> Nolan also avoids using <a href="/wiki/Temp_track" title="Temp track">temp music</a> while cutting his films.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When working with actors, Nolan prefers giving them the time to perform as many takes of a given scene as they want. "I\'ve come to realize that the lighting and camera setups, the technical things, take all the time, but running another take generally only adds a couple of minutes<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... If an actor tells me they can do something more with a scene, I give them the chance, because it\'s not going to cost that much time. It can\'t all be about the technical issues."<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Oldman" title="Gary Oldman">Gary Oldman</a> praised the director for providing a relaxed atmosphere on set, adding, "I\'ve never seen him raise his voice to anyone." He  observed that Nolan would give the actors space to "find things in the scene", and not just give direction for direction\'s sake.<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Branagh" title="Kenneth Branagh">Kenneth Branagh</a> also recognised Nolan\'s ability to provide a harmonious work environment, comparing him with <a href="/wiki/Danny_Boyle" title="Danny Boyle">Danny Boyle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Altman" title="Robert Altman">Robert Altman</a>: "These are not people who try to trick or cajole or hector people. They sort of strip away the chaos."<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nolan chooses to minimize the amount of <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a> for special effects in his films, preferring to use <a href="/wiki/Practical_effects" class="mw-redirect" title="Practical effects">practical effects</a> whenever possible, and only using CGI to enhance elements which he has photographed in camera. For instance, his films <i>Batman Begins</i>, <i>Inception</i>, and <i>Interstellar</i> featured 620, 500, and 850 visual-effects shots, respectively, which is considered minor when compared with contemporary visual-effects epics, which may have upwards of 1,500 to 2,000 VFX shots:<sup id="cite_ref-trussell_199-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trussell-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> "I believe in an absolute difference between animation and photography. However sophisticated your computer-generated imagery is, if it\'s been created from no physical elements and you haven\'t shot anything, it\'s going to feel like animation. There are usually two different goals in a visual effects movie. One is to fool the audience into seeing something seamless, and that\'s how I try to use it. The other is to impress the audience with the amount of money spent on the spectacle of the visual effect, and that, I have no interest in".<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Nolan shoots the entirety of his films with one unit, rather than using a <a href="/wiki/Second_unit" title="Second unit">second unit</a> for action sequences. That way, Nolan keeps his personality and point of view in every aspect of the film. "If I don\'t need to be directing the shots that go in the movie, why do I need to be there at all? The screen is the same size for every shot<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... Many action films embrace a second unit taking on all of the action. For me, that\'s odd because then why did you want to do an action film?"<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">Themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Nolan\'s work explores <a href="/wiki/Existential" class="mw-redirect" title="Existential">existential</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ethics" title="Ethics">ethical</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Epistemology" title="Epistemology">epistemological</a> themes such as subjective experience, distortion of memory, human morality, the nature of time, <a href="/wiki/Causality" title="Causality">causality</a>, and construction of <a href="/wiki/Personal_identity" title="Personal identity">personal identity</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Parks_200-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parks-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup> "I\'m fascinated by our subjective perception of reality, that we are all stuck in a very singular point of view, a singular perspective on what we all agree to be an objective reality, and movies are one of the ways in which we try to see things from the same point of view".<sup id="cite_ref-FoundasInception_188-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoundasInception-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> His films contain a notable degree of <a href="/wiki/Ambiguity" title="Ambiguity">ambiguity</a> and often examine the similarities between filmmaking and architecture.<sup id="cite_ref-WiredNolan_203-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WiredNolan-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> Film critic <a href="/wiki/Tom_Shone" title="Tom Shone">Tom Shone</a> described Nolan\'s oeuvre as "epistemological thrillers whose protagonists, gripped by the desire for definitive answers, must negotiate mazy environments in which the <a href="/wiki/Truth" title="Truth">truth</a> is always beyond their reach."<sup id="cite_ref-Shone2014_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shone2014-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In an essay titled <i>The rational wonders of Christopher Nolan</i>, film critic <a href="/wiki/Mike_D%27Angelo" title="Mike D&#39;Angelo">Mike D\'Angelo</a> argues that the filmmaker is a <a href="/wiki/Materialism" title="Materialism">materialist</a> dedicated to exploring the wonders of the natural world. "Underlying nearly every film he\'s ever made, no matter how fanciful, is his conviction that the universe can be explained entirely by physical processes."<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Impossible_staircase.svg" class="image"><img alt="A staircase in a square format. The stairs make four 90-degree turns in each corner, so they are in the format of a continuous loop." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Impossible_staircase.svg/170px-Impossible_staircase.svg.png" width="170" height="129" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Impossible_staircase.svg/255px-Impossible_staircase.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Impossible_staircase.svg/340px-Impossible_staircase.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="372" data-file-height="283" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Impossible_staircase.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Maze" title="Maze">Mazes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Geometric_shape" title="Geometric shape">geometric shapes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Impossible_object" title="Impossible object">impossible constructions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paradoxes" class="mw-redirect" title="Paradoxes">paradoxes</a> are prominently featured in Nolan\'s work.<sup id="cite_ref-FoundasInception_188-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FoundasInception-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Penrose_stairs" title="Penrose stairs">Penrose stairs</a> featured in <i>Inception</i> as an example of the impossible objects that can be created in <a href="/wiki/Lucid_dream" title="Lucid dream">lucid dream</a> worlds.</div></div></div>\n<p>Apart from the larger themes of <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a> and conspiracy, his characters are often emotionally disturbed, obsessive, and morally ambiguous, facing the fears and anxieties of <a href="/wiki/Loneliness" title="Loneliness">loneliness</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guilt_(emotion)" title="Guilt (emotion)">guilt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jealousy" title="Jealousy">jealousy</a>, and greed. By grounding "everyday neurosis&#160;&#8211;&#32;our everyday sort of fears and hopes for ourselves" in a heightened reality, Nolan makes them more accessible to a universal audience.<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup> The protagonists of Nolan\'s films are often driven by philosophical beliefs, and their fate is ambiguous.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> In some of his films, the protagonist and antagonist are mirror images of each other, a point which is made to the protagonist by the antagonist. Through the clashing of ideologies, Nolan highlights the ambivalent nature of truth.<sup id="cite_ref-Film-philosophy_176-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Film-philosophy-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The director also uses his real-life experiences as an inspiration in his work, saying, "From a creative point of view, the process of growing up, the process of maturing, getting married, having kids, I\'ve tried to use that in my work. I\'ve tried to just always be driven by the things that were important to me."<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> Writing for <i>The Playlist</i>, Oliver Lyttelton singled out <a href="/wiki/Parenting" title="Parenting">parenthood</a> as a signature theme in Nolan\'s work, adding; "the director avoids talking about his private life, but fatherhood has been at the emotional heart of almost everything he\'s made, at least from <i>Batman Begins</i> onwards (previous films, it should be said, pre-dated the birth of his kids)."<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nolan\'s most prominent recurring theme is the concept of <a href="/wiki/Time" title="Time">time</a>. The director has identified that all of his films "have had some odd relationship with time, usually in just a structural sense, in that I have always been interested in the subjectivity of time."<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup> Writing for <i>Film Philosophy</i>, Emma Bell points out that the characters in <i>Inception</i> do not literally time-travel, "rather they escape time by being <i>stricken</i> in it&#160;&#8211;&#32;building the delusion that time has not passed, and is not passing now. They feel time grievously: willingly and knowingly destroying their experience by creating multiple simultaneous existences."<sup id="cite_ref-Film-philosophy_176-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Film-philosophy-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Interstellar</i>, Nolan explored the laws of physics as represented in Einstein\'s theory of <a href="/wiki/General_relativity" title="General relativity">general relativity</a>, identifying time as the film\'s antagonist.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ontology" title="Ontology">Ontological</a> questions concerning the nature of <a href="/wiki/Existence" title="Existence">existence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reality" title="Reality">reality</a> also play a major role in his body of work. Alec Price and M.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>Dawson of <i>Left Field Cinema</i> noted that the <a href="/wiki/Existential_crisis" title="Existential crisis">existential crisis</a> of conflicted male figures "struggling with the slippery nature of identity" is a prevalent theme in Nolan\'s films. The actual (or objective) world is of less importance than the way in which we absorb and remember, and it is this created (or subjective) reality that truly matters. "It is solely in the mind and the heart where any sense of permanency or equilibrium can ever be found."<sup id="cite_ref-Leftfield_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Leftfield-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> According to film theorist Todd McGowan, these "created realities" also reveal the ethical and political importance of creating fictions and falsehoods. Nolan\'s films typically deceive spectators about the events that occur and the motivations of the characters, but they do not abandon the idea of truth altogether. Instead, "They show us how truth must emerge out of the lie if it is not to lead us entirely astray." McGowan further argues that Nolan is the first filmmaker to devote himself entirely to the illusion of the medium, calling him a <a href="/wiki/Hegel" class="mw-redirect" title="Hegel">Hegelian</a> filmmaker.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup> In <i>Inception</i>, Nolan was inspired by <a href="/wiki/Lucid_dreaming" class="mw-redirect" title="Lucid dreaming">lucid dreaming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dream_incubation" title="Dream incubation">dream incubation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> The film\'s characters try to embed an idea in a person\'s mind without their knowledge, similar to <a href="/wiki/Sigmund_Freud" title="Sigmund Freud">Freud\'s</a> theory that the unconscious influences one\'s behavior without one\'s knowledge.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> Most of the film takes place in interconnected dream worlds; this creates a framework where actions in the real (or dream) worlds ripple across others. The dream is always in a state of emergence, shifting across levels as the characters navigate it.<sup id="cite_ref-Paul_214-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Paul-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> Like <i>Memento</i> and <i>The Prestige</i>, <i>Inception</i> uses <a href="/wiki/Metalepsis" title="Metalepsis">metaleptic</a> storytelling devices and follows Nolan\'s "auteur affinity of converting, moreover, converging narrative and cognitive values into and within a fictional story".<sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nolan\'s work has often been the subject of extensive <a href="/wiki/Social_commentary" title="Social commentary">social</a> and <a href="/wiki/Political_criticism" title="Political criticism">political commentary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-216" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> <i>The Dark Knight</i> trilogy explored themes of chaos, terrorism, escalation of violence, financial manipulation, <a href="/wiki/Utilitarianism" title="Utilitarianism">utilitarianism</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mass_surveillance" title="Mass surveillance">mass surveillance</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Class_conflict" title="Class conflict">class conflict</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bordwell2012_173-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bordwell2012-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Post-9/11_220-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Post-9/11-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> Batman\'s arc of rising (philosophically) from a man to "more than just a man" is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Friedrich_Nietzsche" title="Friedrich Nietzsche">Nietzschian</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cbermensch" title="\xc3\x9cbermensch">\xc3\x9cbermensch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> The films also explore ideas akin to <a href="/wiki/Jean-Jacques_Rousseau" title="Jean-Jacques Rousseau">Jean-Jacques Rousseau</a>\'s philosophical glorification of a simpler, more primitive way of life and the concept of <a href="/wiki/General_will" title="General will">general will</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup> Theorist <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Kellner" title="Douglas Kellner">Douglas Kellner</a> saw the series as a critical allegory about the <a href="/wiki/Presidency_of_George_W._Bush" title="Presidency of George W. Bush">Bush\xe2\x80\x93Cheney era</a>, highlighting the theme of government corruption and failure to solve social problems, as well as the cinematic spectacle and iconography related to <a href="/wiki/9/11" class="mw-redirect" title="9/11">9/11</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Conservatism_in_the_United_States" title="Conservatism in the United States">conservative</a> magazine <i><a href="/wiki/The_American_Spectator" title="The American Spectator">The American Spectator</a></i> published an article, <i>In Search of Christopher Nolan</i>, writing, "All of Nolan\xe2\x80\x99s films, while maintaining a strong <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotism</a>, plunges below the surface into the murky waters of philosophy, probing some of the deepest human struggles in our unfortunately <a href="/wiki/Postmodernism" title="Postmodernism">postmodern</a> age."<sup id="cite_ref-AmericanSpectator18_225-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmericanSpectator18-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> The article further argues that <i>Dunkirk</i> echoes the work of absurdist playwrights like <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Beckett" title="Samuel Beckett">Samuel Beckett</a> and the bleak, existential novels of <a href="/wiki/Albert_Camus" title="Albert Camus">Albert Camus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean-Paul_Sartre" title="Jean-Paul Sartre">Jean-Paul Sartre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AmericanSpectator18_225-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AmericanSpectator18-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup> Nolan has said that none of his films are intended to be political.<sup id="cite_ref-Political-2012_226-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Political-2012-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influences">Influences</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Influences">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Escher.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Escher.jpg/170px-Escher.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Escher.jpg/255px-Escher.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Escher.jpg/340px-Escher.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1706" data-file-height="2274" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Escher.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nolan has credited <a href="/wiki/M._C._Escher" title="M. C. Escher">M. C. Escher</a> as a major influence.</div></div></div>\n<p>The filmmaker has often cited <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> <a href="/wiki/Graphic_arts" title="Graphic arts">graphic artist</a> <a href="/wiki/M._C._Escher" title="M. C. Escher">M. C. Escher</a> as a major influence on his own work. "I\'m very inspired by the prints of M.<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>C. Escher and the interesting connection-point or blurring of boundaries between art and science, and art and mathematics."<sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> Another source of inspiration is <a href="/wiki/Argentine" class="mw-redirect" title="Argentine">Argentine</a> writer <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Luis_Borges" title="Jorge Luis Borges">Jorge Luis Borges</a>. The director has called <i>Memento</i> a "strange cousin" to <i><a href="/wiki/Funes_the_Memorious" title="Funes the Memorious">Funes the Memorious</a></i>, and has said, "I think his writing naturally lends itself to a cinematic interpretation because it is all about efficiency and precision, the bare bones of an idea."<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Other filmmakers who Nolan has cited as influences include <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-nolan_comments_on_Stanley_Kubrick_229-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nolan_comments_on_Stanley_Kubrick-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DCR_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCR-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Mann" title="Michael Mann">Michael Mann</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-231" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-231">&#91;231&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Terrence_Malick" title="Terrence Malick">Terrence Malick</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-DCR_230-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DCR-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Orson_Welles" title="Orson Welles">Orson Welles</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lawrence_232-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawrence-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fritz_Lang" title="Fritz Lang">Fritz Lang</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Vejvoda_233-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vejvoda-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Roeg" title="Nicolas Roeg">Nicolas Roeg</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-234" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-234">&#91;234&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Lumet" title="Sidney Lumet">Sidney Lumet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Vejvoda_233-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vejvoda-233">&#91;233&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Lean" title="David Lean">David Lean</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-235" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-235">&#91;235&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley Scott</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Terry_Gilliam" title="Terry Gilliam">Terry Gilliam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Lawrence_232-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lawrence-232">&#91;232&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/John_Frankenheimer" title="John Frankenheimer">John Frankenheimer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-236" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-236">&#91;236&#93;</a></sup> Nolan\'s personal favorite films include <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i> (1982), <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i> (1977), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Man_Who_Would_Be_King_(film)" title="The Man Who Would Be King (film)">The Man Who Would Be King</a></i> (1975), <i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia_(film)" title="Lawrence of Arabia (film)">Lawrence of Arabia</a></i> (1962), <i><a href="/wiki/Chinatown_(1974_film)" title="Chinatown (1974 film)">Chinatown</a></i> (1974), <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey_(film)" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (film)">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i> (1968), and <i><a href="/wiki/Withnail_and_I" title="Withnail and I">Withnail and I</a></i> (1987).<sup id="cite_ref-237" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-237">&#91;237&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-238" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-238">&#91;238&#93;</a></sup> In 2013 Criterion Collection released a list of Nolan\'s ten favorite films from its catalog, which included <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hit_(1984_film)" title="The Hit (1984 film)">The Hit</a></i> (1984), <i><a href="/wiki/12_Angry_Men_(1957_film)" title="12 Angry Men (1957 film)">12 Angry Men</a></i> (1957), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Thin_Red_Line_(1998_film)" title="The Thin Red Line (1998 film)">The Thin Red Line</a></i> (1998), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Testament_of_Dr._Mabuse" title="The Testament of Dr. Mabuse">The Testament of Dr. Mabuse</a></i> (1933), <i><a href="/wiki/Bad_Timing" title="Bad Timing">Bad Timing</a></i> (1980), <i><a href="/wiki/Merry_Christmas_Mr._Lawrence" class="mw-redirect" title="Merry Christmas Mr. Lawrence">Merry Christmas Mr. Lawrence</a></i> (1983), <i><a href="/wiki/For_All_Mankind" title="For All Mankind">For All Mankind</a></i> (1989), <i><a href="/wiki/Koyaanisqatsi" title="Koyaanisqatsi">Koyaanisqatsi</a></i> (1982), <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._Arkadin" title="Mr. Arkadin">Mr. Arkadin</a></i> (1955), and <a href="/wiki/Erich_von_Stroheim" title="Erich von Stroheim">Erich von Stroheim</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Greed_(film)" title="Greed (film)">Greed</a></i> (1924) (unavailable on Criterion).<sup id="cite_ref-239" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-239">&#91;239&#93;</a></sup> He is also a fan of the <i><a href="/wiki/James_Bond_in_film" title="James Bond in film">James Bond</a></i> films,<sup id="cite_ref-240" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-240">&#91;240&#93;</a></sup> citing them as a "a huge source of inspiration" and has expressed his admiration for the work of composer  <a href="/wiki/John_Barry_(composer)" title="John Barry (composer)">John Barry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DesertIsland_241-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DesertIsland-241">&#91;241&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nolan\'s habit for employing non-linear storylines was particularly influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Graham_Swift" title="Graham Swift">Graham Swift</a> novel <i><a href="/wiki/Waterland_(novel)" title="Waterland (novel)">Waterland</a></i>, which he felt "did incredible things with parallel timelines, and told a story in different dimensions that was extremely coherent". He was also influenced by the visual language of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Pink_Floyd_%E2%80%93_The_Wall" title="Pink Floyd \xe2\x80\x93 The Wall">Pink Floyd \xe2\x80\x93 The Wall</a></i> (1982) and the structure of <i><a href="/wiki/Pulp_Fiction_(film)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pulp Fiction (film)">Pulp Fiction</a></i> (1994), stating that he was "fascinated with what <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Tarantino" title="Quentin Tarantino">Tarantino</a> had done".<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> <i>Inception</i> was partly influenced by <a href="/wiki/Dante_Alighieri" title="Dante Alighieri">Dante\'s</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(Dante)" title="Inferno (Dante)">Inferno</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-WiredNolan_203-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WiredNolan-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup> For <i>Interstellar</i>, he mentioned a number of literary influences, including <i><a href="/wiki/Flatland" title="Flatland">Flatland</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Edwin_Abbott_Abbott" title="Edwin Abbott Abbott">Edwin Abbott Abbott</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wasp_Factory" title="The Wasp Factory">The Wasp Factory</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Iain_Banks" title="Iain Banks">Iain Banks</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Madeleine_L%27Engle" title="Madeleine L&#39;Engle">Madeleine L\'Engle</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/A_Wrinkle_in_Time" title="A Wrinkle in Time">A Wrinkle in Time</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-242" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-242">&#91;242&#93;</a></sup> Other influences Nolan has credited include figurative painter <a href="/wiki/Francis_Bacon_(artist)" title="Francis Bacon (artist)">Francis Bacon</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-243" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-243">&#91;243&#93;</a></sup> architect <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Mies_van_der_Rohe" title="Ludwig Mies van der Rohe">Ludwig Mies van der Rohe</a>, and authors <a href="/wiki/Raymond_Chandler" title="Raymond Chandler">Raymond Chandler</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Ellroy" title="James Ellroy">James Ellroy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thompson_(writer)" title="Jim Thompson (writer)">Jim Thompson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Timberg_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Timberg-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens" title="Charles Dickens">Charles Dickens</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/A_Tale_of_Two_Cities" title="A Tale of Two Cities">A Tale of Two Cities</a></i> was a major influence on <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-244" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-244">&#91;244&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Views_on_the_film_industry">Views on the film industry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Views on the film industry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Christopher Nolan is a vocal proponent of the continued use of <a href="/wiki/Film_stock" title="Film stock">film stock</a>, and prefers it over digital recording and projection formats, summing up his belief as, "I am not committed to film out of nostalgia. I am in favor of any kind of technical innovation but it needs to exceed what <i>has</i> gone before and so far nothing has exceeded anything that\'s come before".<sup id="cite_ref-Deadline_245-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Deadline-245">&#91;245&#93;</a></sup> Nolan\'s major concern is that the film industry\'s adoption of digital formats has been driven purely by economic factors as opposed to digital being a superior medium to film, saying, "I think, truthfully, it boils down to the economic interest of manufacturers and [a production] industry that makes more money through change rather than through maintaining the status quo."<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_(25045926926).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_%2825045926926%29.jpg/220px-Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_%2825045926926%29.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_%2825045926926%29.jpg/330px-Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_%2825045926926%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_%2825045926926%29.jpg/440px-Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_%2825045926926%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Colin_Trevorrow_and_Christopher_Nolan_(25045926926).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nolan (right) and director <a href="/wiki/Colin_Trevorrow" title="Colin Trevorrow">Colin Trevorrow</a> discussing the importance of film at the <a href="/wiki/2016_Sundance_Film_Festival" title="2016 Sundance Film Festival">2016 Sundance Film Festival</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Shortly before Christmas of 2011, Nolan invited several prominent directors, including, <a href="/wiki/Edgar_Wright" title="Edgar Wright">Edgar Wright</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Bay" title="Michael Bay">Michael Bay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bryan_Singer" title="Bryan Singer">Bryan Singer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jon_Favreau" title="Jon Favreau">Jon Favreau</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eli_Roth" title="Eli Roth">Eli Roth</a>, <a href="/wiki/Duncan_Jones" title="Duncan Jones">Duncan Jones</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Daldry" title="Stephen Daldry">Stephen Daldry</a>, to Universal CityWalk\'s IMAX theatre for a private screening of the first six minutes of <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, which had been shot on IMAX film and edited from the <a href="/wiki/Original_camera_negative" title="Original camera negative">original camera negative</a>. Nolan used this screening in an attempt to showcase the superiority of the IMAX format over digital, and to warn the filmmakers that unless they continued to assert their choice to use film in their productions, Hollywood movie studios would begin to phase out the use of film in favor of digital.<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-filmvsdigital_246-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-filmvsdigital-246">&#91;246&#93;</a></sup> Nolan explained, "I wanted to give them a chance to see the potential, because I think IMAX is the best film format that was ever invented. It\'s the gold standard and what any other technology has to match up to, but none have, in my opinion. The message I wanted to put out there was that no one is taking anyone\'s digital cameras away. But if we want film to continue as an option, and someone is working on a big studio movie with the resources and the power to insist [on] film, they should say so. I felt as if I didn\'t say anything, and then we started to lose that option, it would be a shame. When I look at a digitally acquired and projected image, it looks inferior against an original negative anamorphic print or an IMAX one."<sup id="cite_ref-Ressner_30-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ressner-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Nolan has lent out IMAX lenses from his personal collection to fellow directors to use on movies such as <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_The_Force_Awakens" title="Star Wars: The Force Awakens">Star Wars: The Force Awakens</a></i> (2015).<sup id="cite_ref-247" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-247">&#91;247&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nolan is also an advocate for the importance of films being shown in large-screen cinema theaters as opposed to home video formats, as he believes that, "The theatrical window is to the movie business what live concerts are to the music business&#160;&#8211;&#32;and no one goes to a concert to be played an MP3 on a bare stage."<sup id="cite_ref-WallStreet_248-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WallStreet-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> In 2014 Christopher Nolan wrote an article for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i> where he expressed concern that as the film industry transitions away from photochemical film towards digital formats, the difference between seeing films in theaters versus on other formats will become trivialised, leaving audiences no incentive to seek out a theatrical experience. Nolan further expressed concern that with content digitised, theaters of the future will be able to track best-selling films and adjust their programming accordingly, a process that favors large heavily marketed studio films, but will marginalise smaller innovative and unconventional pictures. In order to combat this, Nolan believes the industry needs to focus on improving the theatrical experience with bigger and more beautiful presentation formats that cannot be accessed or reproduced in the home, as well as embracing the new generation of aspiring young innovative filmmakers.<sup id="cite_ref-WallStreet_248-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WallStreet-248">&#91;248&#93;</a></sup> As a filmmaker he opposes <a href="/wiki/Motion_interpolation" title="Motion interpolation">motion interpolation</a>, commonly referred to as the "soap opera effect", as the default setting on television.<sup id="cite_ref-AVTV_249-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AVTV-249">&#91;249&#93;</a></sup> In 2018, Nolan and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Thomas_Anderson" title="Paul Thomas Anderson">Paul Thomas Anderson</a> reached out to television manufacturers in an attempt to "try and give directors a voice in how the technical standards of our work can be maintained in the home."<sup id="cite_ref-IndiTV_250-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IndiTV-250">&#91;250&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recurring_collaborators">Recurring collaborators</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Recurring collaborators">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>His wife, <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thomas" title="Emma Thomas">Emma Thomas</a> has co-produced all of his films (including <i>Memento</i>, in which she is credited as an associate producer). He regularly works with his brother, Jonathan Nolan (creator of <i><a href="/wiki/Person_of_Interest_(TV_series)" title="Person of Interest (TV series)">Person of Interest</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Westworld_(TV_series)" title="Westworld (TV series)">Westworld</a></i>), who describes their working relationship in the production notes for <i>The Prestige</i>: "I\'ve always suspected that it has something to do with the fact that he\'s left-handed and I\'m right-handed, because he\'s somehow able to look at my ideas and flip them around in a way that\'s just a little bit more twisted and interesting. It\'s great to be able to work with him like that".<sup id="cite_ref-Prestigeinter1_251-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Prestigeinter1-251">&#91;251&#93;</a></sup> When working on separate projects, the brothers always consult each other.<sup id="cite_ref-252" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-252">&#91;252&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hans_Zimmer_2010_(1).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Hans_Zimmer_2010_%281%29.jpg/190px-Hans_Zimmer_2010_%281%29.jpg" width="190" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Hans_Zimmer_2010_%281%29.jpg/285px-Hans_Zimmer_2010_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Hans_Zimmer_2010_%281%29.jpg/380px-Hans_Zimmer_2010_%281%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2856" data-file-height="2285" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hans_Zimmer_2010_(1).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Composer <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>, one of Nolan\'s most frequent collaborators</div></div></div>\n<div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:246px;&#32;;"><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r856303512"/>\n<div class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">As a director, I\'m sort of a human lens through which everyone\'s efforts are focused. A big part of my job is making decisions about how all the great talent that I\'m working with blends into a single consciousness</div>\n<p><cite class="left-aligned" style="">\xe2\x80\x94Nolan on collaboration and leadership.<sup id="cite_ref-253" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-253">&#91;253&#93;</a></sup></cite>\n</p>\n</div>\n<p>The director has worked with screenwriter David S. Goyer on all his comic-book adaptations.<sup id="cite_ref-254" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-254">&#91;254&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wally_Pfister" title="Wally Pfister">Wally Pfister</a> was the cinematographer for all of Nolan\'s films from <i>Memento</i> to <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-255" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-255">&#91;255&#93;</a></sup> Embarking on his own career as a director, Pfister said: "The greatest lesson I learned from Chris Nolan is to keep my humility. He is an absolute gentleman on set and he is wonderful to everyone&#160;&#8211;&#32;from the actors to the entire crew, he treats everyone with respect."<sup id="cite_ref-256" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-256">&#91;256&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Lee_Smith_(editor)" title="Lee Smith (editor)">Lee Smith</a> has been Nolan\'s editor since <i>Batman Begins</i>, with <a href="/wiki/Dody_Dorn" title="Dody Dorn">Dody Dorn</a> editing <i>Memento</i> and <i>Insomnia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-257" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-257">&#91;257&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Julyan" title="David Julyan">David Julyan</a> composed the music for Nolan\'s early work, while <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a> and <a href="/wiki/James_Newton_Howard" title="James Newton Howard">James Newton Howard</a> provided the music for <i>Batman Begins</i> and <i>The Dark Knight</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-258" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-258">&#91;258&#93;</a></sup> Zimmer scored <i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>, and has worked with Nolan on his subsequent films.<sup id="cite_ref-259" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-259">&#91;259&#93;</a></sup> Zimmer has said his creative relationship with Nolan is highly collaborative, and that he considers Nolan a "co-creator" of the music.<sup id="cite_ref-260" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-260">&#91;260&#93;</a></sup> The director has worked with <a href="/wiki/Sound_editor_(filmmaking)" title="Sound editor (filmmaking)">sound designer</a> <a href="/wiki/Richard_King_(sound_designer)" title="Richard King (sound designer)">Richard King</a> and <a href="/wiki/Re-recording_mixer" title="Re-recording mixer">re-recording mixer</a> <a href="/wiki/Gary_Rizzo" title="Gary Rizzo">Gary Rizzo</a> since <i>The Prestige</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-261" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-261">&#91;261&#93;</a></sup> Nolan has frequently collaborated with special-effects supervisor <a href="/wiki/Chris_Corbould" title="Chris Corbould">Chris Corbould</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-262" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-262">&#91;262&#93;</a></sup> stunt coordinator Tom Struthers<sup id="cite_ref-263" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-263">&#91;263&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Assistant_director" title="Assistant director">first assistant director</a> Nilo Otero,<sup id="cite_ref-264" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-264">&#91;264&#93;</a></sup> and visual effects supervisor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Franklin_(visual_effects_supervisor)" title="Paul Franklin (visual effects supervisor)">Paul Franklin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-265" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-265">&#91;265&#93;</a></sup> Production designer <a href="/wiki/Nathan_Crowley" title="Nathan Crowley">Nathan Crowley</a> has worked with him since <i>Insomnia</i> (except for <i>Inception</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-266" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-266">&#91;266&#93;</a></sup> Nolan has called Crowley one of his closest and most inspiring creative collaborators.<sup id="cite_ref-267" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-267">&#91;267&#93;</a></sup> Casting director <a href="/wiki/John_Papsidera" title="John Papsidera">John Papsidera</a> has worked on all of Nolan\'s films, except <i>Following</i> and <i>Insomnia</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-268" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-268">&#91;268&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Christian_Bale" title="Christian Bale">Christian Bale</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cillian_Murphy" title="Cillian Murphy">Cillian Murphy</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a> have been frequent collaborators since the mid-2000s. Caine is Nolan\'s most prolific collaborator, having appeared in seven of his films, and is regarded by Nolan to be his "good luck charm".<sup id="cite_ref-269" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-269">&#91;269&#93;</a></sup> In return, Caine has described Nolan as "one of cinema\'s greatest directors", comparing him favorably with the likes of <a href="/wiki/David_Lean" title="David Lean">David Lean</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Huston" title="John Huston">John Huston</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_L._Mankiewicz" title="Joseph L. Mankiewicz">Joseph L. Mankiewicz</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-270" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-270">&#91;270&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-271" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-271">&#91;271&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-272" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-272">&#91;272&#93;</a></sup> Nolan is also known for casting stars from the 1980s in his films, i.e. <a href="/wiki/Rutger_Hauer" title="Rutger Hauer">Rutger Hauer</a> (<i>Batman Begins</i>), <a href="/wiki/Eric_Roberts" title="Eric Roberts">Eric Roberts</a> (<i>The Dark Knight</i>), <a href="/wiki/Tom_Berenger" title="Tom Berenger">Tom Berenger</a> (<i>Inception</i>), and <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Modine" title="Matthew Modine">Matthew Modine</a> (<i>The Dark Knight Rises</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-273" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-273">&#91;273&#93;</a></sup> Modine said of working with Nolan, "There are no chairs on a Nolan set, he gets out of his car and goes to the set. And he stands up until lunchtime. And then he stands up until they say \'Wrap\'. He\'s fully engaged&#160;&#8211;&#32;in every aspect of the film."<sup id="cite_ref-274" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-274">&#91;274&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg/220px-Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg/330px-Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg/440px-Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="841" data-file-height="624" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Nolan_and_Emma_Thomas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Nolan and his wife <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thomas" title="Emma Thomas">Emma Thomas</a> in January 2011</div></div></div>\n<p>Nolan is married to <a href="/wiki/Emma_Thomas" title="Emma Thomas">Emma Thomas</a>, whom he met at University College London when he was 19.<sup id="cite_ref-telegraph_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-British_Cinematographer_pt2_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-British_Cinematographer_pt2-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> She has worked as a producer on all of his films, and together they founded the production company <a href="/wiki/Syncopy_Inc." title="Syncopy Inc.">Syncopy Inc.</a><sup id="cite_ref-275" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-275">&#91;275&#93;</a></sup> The couple have four children and reside in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-276" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-276">&#91;276&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes_277-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-277">&#91;277&#93;</a></sup> Protective of his privacy, he rarely discusses his personal life in interviews.<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis-Kraus_278-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-Kraus-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup> However, he has publicly shared some of his sociopolitical concerns for the future, such as the current conditions of nuclear weapons and environmental issues that he says need to be addressed.<sup id="cite_ref-279" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-279">&#91;279&#93;</a></sup> He has also expressed an admiration for <a href="/wiki/Scientific_objectivity" class="mw-redirect" title="Scientific objectivity">scientific objectivity</a>, wishing it were applied "in every aspect of our civilization."<sup id="cite_ref-ThorneNolan_190-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ThorneNolan-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Nolan prefers not to use a mobile phone or an email address,<sup id="cite_ref-280" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-280">&#91;280&#93;</a></sup> saying, "It\'s not that I\'m a <a href="/wiki/Luddite" title="Luddite">Luddite</a> and don\'t like technology; I\'ve just never been interested [...] When I moved to Los Angeles in 1997, nobody really had cell phones, and I just never went down that path."<sup id="cite_ref-281" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-281">&#91;281&#93;</a></sup> He also prohibits use of phones on set.<sup id="cite_ref-cell_phones_on_set_282-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cell_phones_on_set-282">&#91;282&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Having made some of the most influential and popular films of his time,<sup id="cite_ref-283" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-283">&#91;283&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-284" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-284">&#91;284&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-totalfilm_285-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-totalfilm-285">&#91;285&#93;</a></sup> Nolan\'s work has been as "intensely embraced, analyzed and debated by ordinary film fans as by critics and film academics".<sup id="cite_ref-Lewis-Kraus_278-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lewis-Kraus-278">&#91;278&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Descriptions_286-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Descriptions-286">&#91;286&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-guardian3_287-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian3-287">&#91;287&#93;</a></sup> According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wall_Street_Journal" title="The Wall Street Journal">The Wall Street Journal</a></i>, his "ability to combine box-office success with artistic ambition has given him an extraordinary amount of clout in the industry."<sup id="cite_ref-288" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-288">&#91;288&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Geoff_Andrew" title="Geoff Andrew">Geoff Andrew</a> of the <a href="/wiki/British_Film_Institute" title="British Film Institute">British Film Institute</a> (BFI) and regular contributor to the <i><a href="/wiki/Sight_%26_Sound" title="Sight &amp; Sound">Sight &amp; Sound</a></i> magazine, called Nolan "a persuasively inventive storyteller", singling him out as one of the few contemporary filmmakers producing highly personal films within the Hollywood mainstream. He also pointed out that Nolan\'s films are as notable for their "considerable technical virtuosity and visual flair" as for their "brilliant narrative ingenuity and their unusually adult interest in complex philosophical questions".<sup id="cite_ref-289" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-289">&#91;289&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-290" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-290">&#91;290&#93;</a></sup> Film scholar <a href="/wiki/David_Bordwell" title="David Bordwell">David Bordwell</a> compared Nolan to Stanley Kubrick, citing his ability to turn genre movies into both art and event films.<sup id="cite_ref-BordwellDunkirk_181-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BordwellDunkirk-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Film director and critic <a href="/wiki/Mark_Cousins_(film_critic)" title="Mark Cousins (film critic)">Mark Cousins</a> also applauded Nolan for embracing big ideas, "Hollywood filmmakers generally shy away from ideas \xe2\x80\x94 but not Christopher Nolan".<sup id="cite_ref-291" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-291">&#91;291&#93;</a></sup> Scott Foundas of <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i> declared Nolan "the premier big-canvas storyteller of his generation",<sup id="cite_ref-292" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-292">&#91;292&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Justin_Chang" title="Justin Chang">Justin Chang</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> called him "the great <a href="/wiki/Proceduralist" title="Proceduralist">proceduralist</a> of 21st century blockbuster filmmaking, a lover of nuts-and-bolts minutiae."<sup id="cite_ref-293" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-293">&#91;293&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The filmmaker has been praised by many of his contemporaries, and some have cited his work as influencing their own. <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Wyatt" title="Rupert Wyatt">Rupert Wyatt</a> said in an interview that he thinks of Nolan as a "trailblazer<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... he is to be hugely admired as a master filmmaker, but also someone who has given others behind him a stick to beat back the naysayers who never thought a modern mass audience would be willing to embrace story and character as much as spectacle".<sup id="cite_ref-Harding_294-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Harding-294">&#91;294&#93;</a></sup> Kenneth Branagh called Nolan\'s  approach to large-scale filmmaking "unique in modern cinema", adding "regardless of how popular his movies become, he remains an artist and an auteur. I think for that reason he has become a heroic figure for both the audience and the people working behind the camera."<sup id="cite_ref-295" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-295">&#91;295&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michael_Mann_(director)" class="mw-redirect" title="Michael Mann (director)">Michael Mann</a> complimented Nolan for his "singular vision" and called him "a complete auteur".<sup id="cite_ref-ShoneBlogspot_296-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShoneBlogspot-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Roeg" title="Nicolas Roeg">Nicolas Roeg</a> said of Nolan, "[His] films have a magic to them<span class="nowrap">&#160;</span>... People talk about \'commercial art\' and the term is usually self-negating; Nolan works in the commercial arena and yet there\'s something very poetic about his work."<sup id="cite_ref-ShoneBlogspot_296-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ShoneBlogspot-296">&#91;296&#93;</a></sup>  Martin Scorsese identified Nolan as a filmmaker creating "beautifully made films on a big scale",<sup id="cite_ref-297" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-297">&#91;297&#93;</a></sup>\nand <a href="/wiki/Luca_Guadagnino" title="Luca Guadagnino">Luca Guadagnino</a> called him "one of the ultimate auteurs."<sup id="cite_ref-298" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-298">&#91;298&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Damien_Chazelle" title="Damien Chazelle">Damien Chazelle</a> said of Nolan, "This is a filmmaker who has managed, time and again, to make the most seemingly impersonal projects \xe2\x80\x94 superhero epics, deep-space mind-benders \xe2\x80\x94 feel deeply personal".<sup id="cite_ref-299" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-299">&#91;299&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Olivier_Assayas" title="Olivier Assayas">Olivier Assayas</a> said he admired Nolan for "making movies that are really unlike anything else. The way I see it, he has a really authentic voice."<sup id="cite_ref-300" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-300">&#91;300&#93;</a></sup> Discussing the difference between <a href="/wiki/Art_film" title="Art film">art films</a> and big-studio films, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Spielberg" title="Steven Spielberg">Steven Spielberg</a> referred to Nolan\'s <i>Dark Knight</i> series as an example of both;<sup id="cite_ref-301" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-301">&#91;301&#93;</a></sup> he has described <i>Memento</i> and <i>Inception</i> as "masterworks".<sup id="cite_ref-302" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-302">&#91;302&#93;</a></sup> Nolan has also been commended by <a href="/wiki/Quentin_Tarantino" title="Quentin Tarantino">Quentin Tarantino</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Shone2014_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shone2014-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Cameron" title="James Cameron">James Cameron</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-303" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-303">&#91;303&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brad_Bird" title="Brad Bird">Brad Bird</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-304" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-304">&#91;304&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_del_Toro" title="Guillermo del Toro">Guillermo del Toro</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-305" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-305">&#91;305&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Matt_Reeves" title="Matt Reeves">Matt Reeves</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-306" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-306">&#91;306&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Danny_Boyle" title="Danny Boyle">Danny Boyle</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-307" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-307">&#91;307&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Wong_Kar-Wai" class="mw-redirect" title="Wong Kar-Wai">Wong Kar-Wai</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-308" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-308">&#91;308&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Steven_Soderbergh" title="Steven Soderbergh">Steven Soderbergh</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-309" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-309">&#91;309&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sam_Mendes" title="Sam Mendes">Sam Mendes</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-310" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-310">&#91;310&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Werner_Herzog" title="Werner Herzog">Werner Herzog</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-311" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-311">&#91;311&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Matthew_Vaughn" title="Matthew Vaughn">Matthew Vaughn</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-312" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-312">&#91;312&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Thomas_Anderson" title="Paul Thomas Anderson">Paul Thomas Anderson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-313" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-313">&#91;313&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Denis_Villeneuve" title="Denis Villeneuve">Denis Villeneuve</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-314" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-314">&#91;314&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Paul_Greengrass" title="Paul Greengrass">Paul Greengrass</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-315" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-315">&#91;315&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rian_Johnson" title="Rian Johnson">Rian Johnson</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-316" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-316">&#91;316&#93;</a></sup> and others.<sup id="cite_ref-317" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-317">&#91;317&#93;</a></sup> Noted film critic <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kermode" title="Mark Kermode">Mark Kermode</a> complimented the director for bringing "the discipline and ethics of art-house independent moviemaking" to Hollywood blockbusters, calling him "[The] living proof that you don\'t have to appeal to the lowest common denominator to be profitable".<sup id="cite_ref-318" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-318">&#91;318&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013 a survey of seventeen film academics showed that Nolan was among the most studied directors in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-319" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-319">&#91;319&#93;</a></sup> His work has also been recognised as an influence on video games.<sup id="cite_ref-320" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-320">&#91;320&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-321" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-321">&#91;321&#93;</a></sup> Renowned <a href="/wiki/Video_game_design" title="Video game design">video game designer</a> <a href="/wiki/Hideo_Kojima" title="Hideo Kojima">Hideo Kojima</a> compared <i>Dunkirk</i> to his own work: "Its approach to technology in movie making and refusal to rely on defeating one\'s enemies as a portrayal of war, reminds me in many ways of my work on <i><a href="/wiki/Metal_Gear" title="Metal Gear">Metal Gear</a></i> and where I hope to see my next game go".<sup id="cite_ref-322" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-322">&#91;322&#93;</a></sup> Nolan appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">Time</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;s</span> <a href="/wiki/Time_100" title="Time 100">100 most influential people in the world</a> in 2015 and in the <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Celebrity_100" title="Forbes Celebrity 100"><i>Forbes</i> Celebrity 100</a> in 2011 and 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-323" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-323">&#91;323&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-forbes-2011_324-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-forbes-2011-324">&#91;324&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Awards_and_honors">Awards and honors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Christopher_Nolan&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Awards and honors">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_awards_and_nominations_received_by_Christopher_Nolan" title="List of awards and nominations received by Christopher Nolan">List of awards and nominations received by Christopher Nolan</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Christopher_Nolan_TCL.jpg" class="image"><img alt=""
